Sichuan Fellow Association Meets to Raise Relief Funds 145

Yesterday, the Shanghai Sichuan Fellow Association held a standing committee meeting at the association's office to discuss helping the refugees displaced in the Red areas of northern Sichuan. In addition to all the members of the committee attending, He Baoheng, Zi Zhong, and Li Shenpei, the representatives of the petitioners for the Red disaster in northwestern Sichuan, attended and explained the Red disaster in detail. According to the representatives, more than two-thirds of the people in more than a dozen counties in northern Sichuan have fled due to the Red bandits making a comeback. There are now more than two million refugees gathered in the east and west of Sichuan. The refugee shelters set up by charitable organizations in various places are full, and food is also in short supply, with a tendency to be insecure in the morning and evening. The Red bandits learned of this situation and used various methods to lure the refugees back to their hometowns to be used by them. If they are not quickly relieved and settled, the weak will die in the trenches, and the strong will inevitably be absorbed by the Red bandits. If the other party gets the help of this large number of good people, it will be like a tiger with wings, and the situation will sit down. It is conceivable that the danger is unimaginable. The association is deeply concerned about the lives of more than two million people in Sangzi and the safety of the entire Sichuan. It is deeply feared that the Red Army's conspiracy will trap Sichuan in the second Jiangxi. Therefore, seven measures were decided, and several important cases were discussed. The resolutions are as follows: ㈠ The Chongqing Relief Committee sent a telegram and sent representatives to the meeting to explain the disaster situation of the Red disaster in northern Sichuan, and asked the association to raise funds for relief. The resolutions were: (A) Send a telegram to the Executive Yuan of the National Government and the Disaster Relief Committee, requesting a large amount of relief money to relieve the refugees displaced in the Red areas of more than a dozen counties in northern Sichuan. (B) Send a letter to various charitable organizations and philanthropists in this port, requesting relief. (C) Send a letter to Chinese members of the Central Committee and people from all walks of life in Beijing and Shanghai, requesting them to report to the Central Government and the Yuan and appeal to philanthropists in Beijing and Shanghai. (D) Send Zhong Hangsu, Qiu Zhuozhong, Li Qingfan, and three representatives, together with the representatives of the petitioning group for the Red disaster in northwestern Sichuan, to meet with Wu Tiecheng, the mayor of the city, at 10:00 AM next Tuesday, and ask him to advocate the formation of a fundraising and relief agency by officials and civilians. (E) Schedule a joint reception with the representatives of the petitioning group for reporters, charitable organizations, and philanthropists in this city to report the disaster situation and ask for publicity and assistance. (F) Organize a special committee for fundraising to specialize in raising donations and handling relief matters, and temporarily hire Li Qingfan, Yu Yuanhui, Qiu Zhizhong, Zheng Yushu, Li Xunfu, Shao Jizhen, and Bi Yaquan as members. (G) The various matters decided today will be telegraphed to the Chongqing Relief Committee, Pan Wenhua, and others. ㈡ Can the Executive Committee member and Director of the Publishing Committee, Xie Zhaohua, return to Sichuan to represent the association in calling for peace in the Sichuan War and suppressing the Red Army to secure Sichuan? The resolution was: passed. ㈢ Zhong Hangsu, a member of the Executive Committee of the Association, is now practicing as a lawyer. Can he be hired as the legal counsel of the Association? The resolution was: passed. ㈣ The Shanghai All Circles Clearing and National Salvation Donation Committee asked the Association to reply with the amount of damage to the funds in order to clarify the truth. The resolution was: hand over the documents for verification and reply. ㈤ The Post Office Administration replied to the Association, saying that the postal items detained in Zinei, Sichuan, have been ordered to the Xichuan Post Office to verify and report on how to deal with them. The resolution was: hand over the original letter to Li Xunfu and other members of the business community to pass on to the members of the business community. ㈥ Should a letter of thanks be sent to Shen Bao for publishing the Association's documents and telegrams? The resolution was: passed.

The Ministry of Industry Stipulates the Business License Fee for the Exchange 146

The fee should also be paid for the renewal of the business after the expiration.

Yesterday, the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce informed the various exchanges by order of the Social Bureau transferring the order of the Ministry of Industry, saying that on the ninth of this month, the Shanghai Municipal Social Bureau issued an instruction saying, "For the matter of returning the order, the implementation rules of the Exchange Law have not been stipulated for the business license fee of the exchange. Now, the Ministry has formulated that when the exchange is approved for establishment and a special business tax certificate is issued, the tax certificate fee is set at 500 yuan. The Administrative Yuan's instruction No. 2090 stated, "The presentation is known and approved for the record, and the Ministry's order shall be announced and implemented." This order, and so on, is hereby issued to the various exchanges to know and comply with. This order, and so on, is hereby issued to the various exchanges for reference. Sincerely, the Chinese Cotton Cloth Securities, Goods, Chinese Securities, Miscellaneous Grains, Sesame Cakes, and Gold Exchanges.

Methods for Small Steamers Carrying Passengers and Cargo 147

The Ministry of Transportation, recognizing the numerous dangers arising from the unrestricted carriage of passengers and cargo on small steamers, has formulated regulations to limit such carriage. It has issued a special order to all navigation bureaus and offices to instruct all small steamers to comply with these regulations in order to ensure the safety of passengers and cargo. The regulations are listed below: Regulations on Limiting Passenger and Cargo Capacity of Small Steamers: (1) After inspection and measurement by the competent navigation authority, and determination of the positions and quantities for passenger and cargo loading, small steamers shall be issued a "Passenger and Cargo Permit." The person in charge of the vessel shall indicate the designated passenger and cargo areas inside the permit, using copper or enamel plates, or paint, to mark the vessel's openings (such as "Passenger Cabin," "Cargo Hold," "Engine Room," "Crew Quarters," etc.). The areas designated by the competent navigation authority (such as "This room is permitted to carry only [number] passengers," "No cargo allowed here," "No passengers or cargo allowed here," "Only [amount] of cargo allowed here," etc.) shall also be clearly marked in paint in conspicuous locations. (2) On small steamers carrying both passengers and cargo, the lower deck shall be prohibited for passenger accommodation, and the top of the cabins and engine rooms shall not be used for cargo. Aisles on both sides or in the middle, as well as the boiler room, engine room, steering room, and other important areas, shall be prohibited for carrying passengers or cargo. (3) Small steamers shall not install gangplanks on both sides of the hull for walking or other purposes. Parcels, poultry cages, and other obstacles shall not be hung on the bow or sides of the ship. (4) Small steamers shall carry the following documents and keep them on board at all times: (A) Small Steamer License; (B) Steamer Tonnage Certificate; (C) Ship Inspection Certificate and Ship Inspection Log; (D) Small Steamer Passenger and Cargo Permit. Documents A and B shall be mounted in frames and displayed in a conspicuous location on the ship.

These regulations shall be implemented in accordance with the Regulations on Measurement, Inspection, Registration, and Licensing of Small Steamers, the Ship Inspection Regulations, the Ship Measurement Regulations, and the Regulations on the Management of Towboats and Barges.

### Municipal Chamber of Commerce Notifies Various Trade Associations 152

Invoices and ledgers from November 1, 1929 onward should be checked and stamp duties supplemented.

The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce sent a letter to various trade associations yesterday, stating, "This Chamber telegraphed the Ministry of Finance, requesting that merchants and residents in the concession be advised to supplement the full amount of stamp duties on invoices and ledgers with underpaid stamps to avoid investigation and penalties. The Ministry replied: 'Received your telegram. All shops in the Shanghai Concession should affix stamp duties to invoices and ledgers created after November 1, 1929, before delivery or use, as required by regulations. If, at that time, they disregarded the regulations and failed to affix them, they should immediately supplement the full amount before discovery to avoid penalties. As for the stamp affixing procedure, it is extremely simple, so there is no need to set a supplementation period. Furthermore, the inspection office should regularly inspect new and old documents in accordance with regulations and should not suspend its duties due to [something]. The request is denied.' This has been communicated to the Chamber. Please inform your members to promptly check invoices and ledgers from November 1, 1929 onward and quickly supplement any missing or insufficient stamp duties."

### Special Article 160

Draft Rural Revitalization Plan of the Municipal Social Bureau (Continued)

Second Revitalization Plan

1. Adjusting Rural Finance: Due to various reasons, rural finance is most easily concentrated in urban areas, causing the rural economy to wither and making it difficult for all undertakings to develop. To revitalize rural finance, it is necessary to first pay attention to the adjustment of rural finance and to establish more rural financial institutions to lend directly or indirectly to farmers, so that the finance concentrated in cities can flow to the countryside. In this way, urban and rural finance will be like the flow of liquids, circulating endlessly without any imbalance. The methods are: (A) Establishing a Farmers' Bank: A Farmers' Bank is a financial institution that supports the economic development of farmers and supplements their economic shortcomings. In foreign countries, it is often called an Agricultural and Industrial Bank, because in addition to farmers, it is also necessary to support a part of small industries. In China, 80% of the population are farmers, so establishing a Farmers' Bank is relatively simple and meets the needs. The business of the Farmers' Bank is to lend to farmers at low interest rates, and the farmers use the money to purchase plowing cattle, fertilizers, seeds, etc., to engage in farming. After harvesting, they sell the agricultural products to repay the loan. If unfortunately there are natural disasters or man-made misfortunes and the harvest is poor, making it impossible to repay, they can wait until the following year. This is the characteristic of the Farmers' Bank. There are very few Farmers' Banks in various parts of our country. The Jiangsu Provincial Farmers' Bank is the most scaled among them. According to the report for the year 20, the bank has been established for four years, with 20 branches and a capital of 2 million yuan. Although it cannot be said that it has brought much benefit to the 30 million farmers in Jiangsu, it is a new venture and there are many difficulties in running it, so it is not easy to achieve such results. Although there are poverty relief and agricultural loans in this city, farmers actually benefit very little, because its capital is not much and there are restrictions on lending. Therefore, the poverty relief loan office should expand its capital and form a Farmers' Bank to lend to farmers as much as possible in order to adjust rural funds. (B) Establishing Agricultural Warehouses: Agricultural warehouses can adjust prices and activate finance, which is of great benefit to farmers. It has long been popular in Eastern and Western countries, and the effect is quite significant. The biggest source of wealth in rural areas is the income from agricultural products. The prices of agricultural products often fall after the harvest due to oversupply in the market, and unscrupulous merchants and local tyrants take the opportunity to monopolize and speculate. Farmers are forced to sell their year's hard-earned harvest in pain because of the urgent need for cash, and they cannot wait for a good price. Farmers' income is greatly reduced. If there are agricultural warehouses, farmers can store their agricultural products in the warehouse and wait for a good price. At the same time, the agricultural warehouse issues warehouse receipts, which can be used as collateral for cash. Farmers in this city are oppressed by the urban economy, and this warehouse equipment is particularly needed. Therefore, each district should plan to establish one in order to adjust rural finance.

2. Revitalization of Rural Construction: There are many matters that need to be constructed in rural areas, and the most important are: (A) Dredging Rivers and Improving Farmland Water Conservancy: The rivers in the farmland of this city are either silted up or narrow, and this is the case everywhere. Whenever there is a heavy rain or continuous rain, they are often submerged due to poor discharge. Agricultural crops are either withered or damaged, affecting crop yields and reducing economic income. Therefore, the rivers in each district that are silted up should be dredged, and the narrow ones should be expanded, or new rivers should be opened up to facilitate farmland drainage and increase agricultural output. (B) Building Roads and Dikes to Facilitate Rural Transportation and Prevent River Tides: Although this city belongs to an area with convenient transportation, once you get to the countryside, the roads are narrow and it is difficult for vehicles and horses to travel. The transportation of agricultural products is quite inconvenient, which reduces sales and greatly affects the prices of agricultural products. Therefore, rural roads should be tidied up and built to facilitate transportation. Also, this city borders the river and the sea, and is often subject to tidal surges, which cause dikes to break, flooding fields and endangering rural lives and property. Therefore, dikes should be built to protect against floods. (C) Building New Villages to Set Examples: Improving rural life and revitalizing the economy are not matters that can be accomplished overnight. The government should delineate appropriate areas in the countryside and build a model new village, and earnestly implement improvements in all aspects, such as improving agricultural affairs, preventing pests and diseases, promoting sideline industries, organizing cooperatives, adjusting finance, and improving all construction aspects, to establish a model for rural areas in this city, so that rural areas in each district can follow suit and complete the rural revival (end)

Air Defense 161

— Hualing

It is said that in the Second World War, everyone will [go high and go far], fighting in the [clouds]. Therefore, the Italian planes, touring the United States, caused great stimulation to the Americans. The Japanese can climb to the roof with their air defense forces in two minutes and open anti-aircraft guns in the darkness of the city, and they feel safe enough in air defense. Moreover, it is said that in the next war, throwing a few incendiary bombs or 500-pound bombs is not a good show; you have to show off your magic weapon and play with [poison gas bombs].

[Going high and going far] is naturally cheaper. Airplanes and anti-aircraft guns, like the ancient relics of the Forbidden City, are equally cherished and precious in China. Japanese planes are not at all admiring. However, watching the Tokyo air defense exercise, three [hypothetical enemy] [hypothetical planes] came leisurely and left triumphantly. The defense forces hid on the roof and fired anti-aircraft guns, but did not shoot down any [spoils]. Instead, they discovered the danger that there were too few shelters for the people and that the tap water pipes were buried too shallowly. Japan is extremely uneasy about the [hypothetical enemy] on the other side of the Pacific Ocean, but unexpectedly, the [Japanese hypothetical enemy] on the west coast of the Pacific Ocean, seeing the success of the Italian planes, is also greatly concerned. It can be seen that it is still relatively easy to drive a plane to [shit] in other people's territory. It is somewhat difficult to prevent enemy planes from [shitting], or to make them not dare to come to [shit].

Under the air defense exercise, the air defense forces are already a little unable to cope with [incendiary bombs]. If they really play with [poison gas bombs] in the future, although everyone will wear cigarette cans on their mouths, or be more sophisticated and put gas masks on the faces of cattle, sheep, cats, and dogs, these methods of [thieves leaving the door] will not scare away the enemy planes, nor will they have the ability to display the enemy planes as [spoils]. Therefore, so-called [air defense] is, in my opinion, just that.

Boating in the Riva Litta Village 162

— Dong Kegan

The azure night, like dew, covers the river like a blue cloth belt. The Riva Litta Village, under the high, bright sky, opens its intoxicating eyes.

Bathing in the bright moonlight, on the river shimmering with silver scales, the small boat floats gently.

There is no hissing of cicadas. There is no singing of nightingales. The surroundings are condensed into a realm of tranquility. Occasionally, a sound of sculling comes from the water, like the morning bell of a lonely mountain temple, echoing the low cry of the lonely geese of the night.

Such a big, round silver plate floats beside the boat, unable to be scooped up or broken. Is it the moon falling from the sky? Or is it the dressing mirror thrown down by the girl?

The wind brings jazz music from the village, shattering the virgin beauty of the quiet river like a devil!

Putting down the oars, I and she lie on the deck, looking at the blue sky, white clouds, big moon, and the stars like goldfish eggs. The small boat flows with the water. Flowing like skating, boat! Follow the flowing water, flow to the kingdom without jazz music, without the fragrance of women, without man-eating devils!

Making dreamlike memories under the weeping willows, singing lowly...

Key Tips for Modern Women's Adornment (Part 1) 163

— Bingyu

For modern women, regardless of whether they are from the East or the West, the essential requirements for inner beauty are perming their hair, shaping their eyebrows, applying lipstick, and painting their nails. I have already discussed hairstyles last month. Now, I will introduce the three aspects of shaping eyebrows, applying lipstick, and painting nails in detail. In general, fashionable women who understand these key points can steal the show and be admired everywhere.

Key Points for Shaping Eyebrows

Among makeup techniques, shaping eyebrows and applying lipstick are the most difficult. If the makeup is not done properly, it will not only fail to enhance beauty but will also reveal ugliness, reducing the original attractiveness. This is something we often see in social gatherings and dance halls. So how can one enhance their beauty? To put it simply, everyone should consider the shape of their facial features and correct any shortcomings to maintain their original charm and add a special appeal. For example, for people with broad foreheads and large eyes, drawing thin, elongated eyebrows would be very inappropriate. For people with delicate foreheads, small, pointed eyes, and flat cheeks, drawing curved, thin eyebrows can add a special beauty. Currently, the six most popular eyebrow styles worldwide are: first, the "Dietrich" (named after a German actress) eyebrow, with the eyebrow head pointing downwards and the tail slanting upwards, with the eyebrow line becoming thinner from thick; second, the "figure-eight" eyebrow, with no sharp angles at the eyebrow head and curved parallel to the eyes; third, the "willow leaf" eyebrow, shaped like a willow leaf, slanting upwards from the corner of the eye near the nose; fourth, the "Jizo" eyebrow, with a slight curve, the eyebrow head being higher and gradually sloping down to the eyebrow tail; fifth, the "moth" eyebrow, shaped like the eyebrows of a silkworm moth; and sixth, the "wave" eyebrow, with a short, curved eyebrow line. All of the above six eyebrow shapes require surgery to modify and move the position of the original eyebrows, and they should be drawn according to each person's facial features, the width of the forehead, the size and slope of the eyes, the length and height of the nose, the distance between the eyes, and the distance between the eyebrows and the hairline. For people with long, thin faces, high, narrow nose bridges, and small eyes, drawing the Jizo eyebrow is the most suitable. For people with round faces, drawing the figure-eight eyebrow can show off their beauty, because people with round faces have their hair and eyebrows close together. If the position of the eyebrows is not moved to a suitable place, the face will appear even shorter and wider. People with narrow foreheads and long faces will make their faces appear even longer if they draw thick, short wave eyebrows. Therefore, when choosing eyebrows, be sure to consider the shape of the face, the position of the eyebrows, and the distance between the facial features. In general, when foreign women go to beauty salons for makeup, they first ask the makeup artist to point out the shortcomings of their facial features, then consider the position of their facial features, and choose a suitable eyebrow shape. Modern women in Shanghai don't understand their own shortcomings and simply imitate others, drawing eyebrow shapes randomly. As a result, they detract from their original charm. This point should be paid special attention to!

Key Points for Applying Lipstick

The magic of lips has been fully demonstrated in movies. When the heat of love between men and women in the world reaches its peak, the lips of the man and woman will definitely feel like magnets attracting each other. Therefore, lip makeup is particularly important. In the past, ancient Chinese women only knew how to apply rouge. The so-called cherry red at that time was to apply a cherry-shaped red dot on the middle of the upper and lower lips with rouge. This cherry red could evoke a sense of beauty. Nowadays, the full-lip red style that has been passed down from the West will definitely reveal an extremely ugly state if the secret is not understood.

Northeast Fourth Company Commander 164

— Zhang Henshui

Chapter Thirteen: Abandoning Post to See Soulmate, Beauty Quietly Approves; Inheriting Family Fortune, Strong Man Celebrates Wildly

The two left the shop and returned to their respective camps. The next day at noon, Guan Yaowu went to Yang's house to visit Old Mrs. Yang. He had only called out "Aunt" once in the courtyard when he heard Jiang's voice from inside the house, "Come in. I figured you'd be coming." Guan Yaowu was surprised. "How did she know I was coming today?" He lifted the curtain and went inside. Jiang invited him to sit in the inner room. Guan Yaowu laughed, "How are you, Aunt? I've been busy and haven't been able to visit you. Where's our cousin?" Jiang smiled slightly and said, "She's hiding." Guan Yaowu was even more puzzled. Why would she hide? Jiang took out a box of cigarettes from a drawer in the small table. The cigarette pack was unopened, clearly newly bought. She picked up an old porcelain teapot from the edge of the white stove in the middle of the room, poured a cup of tea, and placed it on the table. The color of the tea also indicated it was freshly brewed. Everything was newly prepared, not just something they happened to have. He realized that Jiang and her daughter knew he was coming. But how did they know? This was strange. He smiled and asked Jiang, "I heard you went to Beijing for a trip. How long has it been since you've been there? Has the city changed much?" Jiang replied, "It's pretty much the same. Cousin, you're a busy man. We're family, so it's always good to talk things over. Don't you want to drink our girl's winter melon soup? Just say what you came for." Guan Yaowu laughed, "Since you've guessed it, there's no point in denying it. I originally heard that Aunt was in favor of this marriage, but why did you suddenly become indifferent?" Jiang sat on a square stool by the window, lifted the piece of paper covering the small glass pane, and looked outside. After looking, she lowered her voice and smiled at Guan Yaowu, "Don't you know the reason for that? It's because he's a soldier and away from home a lot. Besides, although there's the prospect of promotion and wealth in the future, this kind of job isn't as stable as other jobs after all." (157)

Urban Vignettes 165

— Ren Ying

A group of young heroes of the street gather at the corner, fighting over their rights like warlords fighting for territory. On the cement pavement, they fiercely attack each other. Small fists swing, and hot sweat drips from their dirty skin, leaving dark ink marks on their chests. A semi-modern woman walks out of the alley, fixing her gaze on these two fighting heroes and shouting to stop their quarrel. "You little rascals, be careful or I'll tell your uncles." The two young heroes who were fighting so hard stop and lean against the corner of the wall across the alley, silent with sheepish faces. This is more powerful than a declaration to abolish civil war.

A deformed beggar arches his hands on the crowded street, putting on an embarrassing crying face, begging for alms from the young masters and ladies. Soon, a large pile of copper coins accumulates. Not far away, a similar loafer, wearing an Indian silk short shirt and pants, pulls down his high collar, exposing his chest. He walks up to the beggar, moves the copper coins to the other side, and wraps them in old newspaper. Someone says, "This is the profession of some people in Shanghai, far better than the average laborer who works all day."

At the tram stop, there are often several six- or seven-year-old children clinging to your chest, asking you to buy an evening newspaper. "Sir, thank you, won't you buy one?" Many people who were not planning to buy a newspaper often take out their money because of this. A friend told me, "This is someone's doing." But for an innocent, unspoiled child, just the fact that he is being instructed is enough for us to pity him!

Passing the middle of ×× Road, in a place fenced off with bamboo to build a cinema and dance hall, a tin advertising sign is nailed up outside, "Comfort for the heart, comfort for the body." It tells us this so blatantly. No wonder today's movies have no educational meaning and only seek sensual pleasure. Dance halls also don't include any social interaction or entertainment but only seek sexual release. I finally felt lost and bewildered, perhaps this is a vague snapshot of the city.

In Front of My Wife 166

— Chao Shen

In front of your wife, don't always wear a frown, exaggerating the difficulties of dealing with partners.

In front of your wife, don't see her only as a wife who bears your children, but as a lover who regulates your life. In front of your wife, don't make married life too bland, but rather make life more tortuous and interesting.

In front of your wife, you should often tell one or two new jokes to elicit a gentle smile from her.

In front of your wife, never mention any close friendships with any female friends.

In front of your wife, never praise the beauty of any other woman. In front of your wife, you should often praise the admirable aspects of your wife.

Thunderstorm 167

— Hu Xiaomi

In the afternoon, there was a faint rumble of thunder in the sky. The weather was particularly stuffy. Dark clouds quickly gathered from all directions, thick and low, and soon covered up the scorching sun. The sky appeared very frightening, dark and gloomy, as if it were about to collapse.

People felt unusually agitated, their chests felt like they were carrying something weighing millions of pounds, making it hard to breathe.

The sound of thunder echoed back and forth in the dense clouds, and lightning flashed out of the clouds from time to time. The tops of the trees were silent from the cicadas' chirping, only a large group of dragonflies flitted back and forth in the courtyard.

Suddenly, with a crack of thunder, the sky seemed to explode. Raindrops the size of soybeans shot down like a rain of arrows, falling on the sun-scorched ground and turning into rising vapor.

The heavy rain lashed down like arrows, filling the ears with surging sound. The thunder rolled louder in the clouds, and lightning flashed back and forth between the clouds.

An old farmer smiled, watching the sky with his pipe in his mouth, and said, "With this rain, there should be a good harvest this autumn."

The dark clouds slowly dispersed, and the rain gradually stopped. The cicadas chirped loudly in the treetops, and sunlight shone back down to the ground through the clouds. The surging sounds disappeared, and the air seemed excessively quiet.

A few cool breezes blew after the rain, making me feel exceptionally good. I once fell in love with a girl,

That girl wore clothes as blue as the sky,

That girl's eyes were like stars in an autumn night,

That girl's soul was as pure as a full moon. - Where is that girl? - She asked in a sour tone, - Don't be angry! That girl is you! -

- - Red clouds flew onto her cheeks, and she buried her head in my arms, laughing softly:

- What an adorable child! Mischievous, mischievous!

Kissing her red lips, a taste like chewing fresh fruit! - So sweet!

Several small boats, like swallows skimming the water, glided past, and the people on board were also so happy, whistling and singing serenades.

Summer, a happy season! On the river in the village of Valida, my dried-up, nineteen-year-old heart flower has been irrigated with sweet dew and is blooming vigorously!

The details of the meeting are recorded as follows:

Attendees 169

The attendees included Mayor Wu Tiecheng, Central Bank President Kong Xiangxi, Municipal Chamber of Commerce Chairman Wang Xiaolai, Belgian Consul in Shanghai Tan Erfu, American Vice Consul Allen, Health Bureau Director Li Ting'an, Public Security Bureau Director Wen Hongsi, Public Utilities Bureau Director Xu Peihuang, Public Works Bureau Director Shen Yi, British Boxer Indemnity Committee Xu Heshi, Jiaotong University Li Zhaohuan, Guanghua University Zhang Shouyong, Shanghai Art College Liu Haisu, Fudan University Huang Yingsu, Municipal Bureau of Education Zeng Shengdian, World Chinese Students' Federation Zhu Shaoping, Vocational Education Society Pan Yangyao, American Returned Students Association Cao Yunxiang, Zhongshan Cultural Education Center Li Dachao, Joint Association of University Faculty Kang Xuanyi, Joint Association of Secondary School Faculty Xu Zeyi, Shen Bao Ma Chonggan, Shi Shi Xin Bao Jiang Xiangze, Xinwen Bao Hou Xuanqing, Min Bao Zhu Yixin, Continental Bao Xu Xingchu, Pudong Middle School Xu Xizhi, Municipal Education Association Hou Zeyu, Jinan University Yang Yufen, Shang Bao Wu Zhimin, Datong Meng Shouchun, Beixin Xu Wancheng, Zhonghua Lufei, etc., and over three hundred students including Liu Liangman, Zhu Ruhua, and Feng Xigeng, making it a grand occasion.

Proceedings of the Meeting 170

At 4:00 PM, the Public Security Bureau Military Band played music to open the meeting. Mayor Wu Tiecheng served as Chairman, with Zhu Shaoping and Hu Qibing as the chief hosts for foreign guests, and Wu Deyin as the chief host for students. Huang Jingwan, Xu Wancheng, Wu Baojin, Hua Xin'an, Hu Yunxing, Yang Yufen, Kang Xuanyi, and over twenty others served as hosts. First, Chairman Mayor Wu delivered the opening speech, followed by speeches from Kong Xiangxi, Li Zhaohuan, Zhang Shouyong, Wang Xiaolai, and Cao Yunxiang. Then, student representative Liu Liangzhan from Jiaotong University gave a response speech. Tea and snacks were served, followed by entertainment and photography before the meeting adjourned.

Speech by Mayor Wu 171

In his opening speech, Chairman Mayor Wu Tiecheng stated that today, over thirty cultural organizations are sending off the students who are going abroad to study. These thirty-odd organizations include the Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Education, the World Chinese Students' Federation, Jiaotong University, Jinan University, Tongji University, Shanghai Business College, Fudan University, Guanghua University, Shanghai Art College, Pudong Middle School, Qixiu Girls' School, Shen Bao, Xinwen Bao, Shi Shi Xin Bao, Continental Bao, Da Wan Bao, Chen Bao, Min Bao, Zhonghua Daily, China Weekly Review, Shanghai Municipal Education Association, Vocational Education Society, Tsinghua Alumni Association, Chinese-American Cooperation Association, International Affairs Research Association, Joint Association of University Faculty, Joint Association of Secondary School Faculty, Commercial Press, China Publishing House, World Book Company, Beixin Book Company, and Datong Book Company. Now that you are about to leave the motherland and go abroad to study, I would like to take this opportunity, on behalf of the thirty-two cultural organizations and the citizens of Shanghai, to share a few words with you as parting words. The significance of sending you off this year is greater than in previous years. This year, the hopes of the people of the whole country for you are also deeper than in previous years, because China has faced many national crises in recent years. The more national crises there are, the heavier the responsibility of the people becomes. People think more about the future of the country. Thinking about the future of the country, they naturally think about the youth, because whether today we can save the country from its difficulties and make the nation turn from weak to strong depends entirely on the youth of the whole country, especially the youth who have received higher education. China is in a serious position today, all because in the past, education was not universal, not applicable, and not sound, resulting in the people's actions not being unified and consistent. In the current situation of educational decline and cultural immaturity, building a new China is an urgent task. But building a new China must have considerable talent for construction. Here, we cannot help but hope for the youth, especially the youth who go abroad to seek higher learning. I would like to represent the thirty-odd cultural organizations and the citizens in holding endless hopes for you who are going abroad.

Speech by Kong Xiangxi 172

Central Bank President Kong Xiangxi stated that the purpose of your going abroad is to seek knowledge and to seek foreign knowledge. But seeking knowledge must be seeking practical knowledge to achieve your goal. Foreign knowledge has good and bad aspects. We should certainly learn the good aspects, but not all good knowledge is necessarily practical. We should choose the knowledge that is relevant to practice in order to be of benefit to our country, so that the purpose of going abroad to study is not in vain. At the same time, while you are abroad, you must be real Chinese people. China has its own geography, history, and culture. We must always show that we are Chinese people and not be Westernized in order to win honor for our motherland. Today, we are holding a send-off gathering. In the future, when you have completed your studies and returned to the country, we will hold a grand welcome gathering. Its significance will be even greater than today.

Speech by Li Zhaohuan 173

Jiaotong University President Li Zhaohuan stated that I was also a Chinese student who went abroad to study more than ten years ago, but since returning to the country, our country has not been on track in terms of politics, education, and all other construction undertakings. As for what the results will be when you go abroad, it all depends on how much progress China can make after you return in the future. China currently needs construction. The elements of construction are capital and talent. It goes without saying that China lacks capital, but there is also a lack of talent for construction. You are going abroad to study, hoping to seek knowledge to build China. There are thirty-two organizations at today's send-off gathering, and in the future, there may be more than three hundred at the welcome gathering.

Speech by Zhang Shouyong 174

Guanghua University President Zhang Shouyong stated that I am very honored to represent Guanghua University and the Joint Association of University Faculty in attending this send-off gathering for students going abroad. I have never been abroad in my life and have very little knowledge, but my son has been abroad and I have sent him off, but it was not as lively and interesting as today. Speaking of Chinese education, it has indeed made great progress in recent years, but unfortunately, it cannot be connected one by one like building a house. The responsibility for this connection rests entirely on the students who are going abroad today. Therefore, I believe that we should take the essence of European and American countries and use it to build China, not just copy them. If we do this, whether it is national politics or the great masses of society, there will be a way. Your trip is extremely important. I hope you will not fail to make it a success. [Photo of the send-off gathering for students going abroad yesterday (Xu Tianzhang)]

Speech by Wang Xiaolai 175

Municipal Chamber of Commerce Chairman Wang Xiaolai stated that today I received invitations from two places, one from the German warship Longhao and one from here. But after my personal consideration, I felt that sending off the students going abroad was more important than visiting the Longhao, because the two hundred-odd of you going abroad are equivalent to two hundred-odd Longhao cruisers going abroad.

Speech by Cao Yunxiang 176

Former Tsinghua University President Cao Yunxiang stated that China's first student to go abroad was Rong Hong, who went abroad in 1854, more than eighty years ago. At that time, no one sent him off. Currently, people generally say that students who have studied abroad cannot do anything. In fact, Rong Hong, the first student to study abroad, has already done a great job, such as the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company and the Telegraph Administration, which were all Mr. Rong's undertakings. Secondly, the first batch of people to go abroad consisted of four people, two of whom were Ms. Song Qingling and Ms. Song Meiling. These two students can also be considered great people. There was also Mr. Chen Jintao, who also went abroad in this batch. Mr. Chen returned from studying abroad and became a successful economist. He once said that it is very easy to write economic papers, but it is impossible to solve China's major problems by relying on papers. It can be seen that China's problems are great, not that students who have studied abroad have failed. China's first student to study abroad, Rong Hong, said that the solution to China's problems requires the people to be aware, so I hope that you will also make the people aware and bring benefits to the people in the future, and continue the spirit of the first student to study abroad.

Response Speech by Liu Liangzhan 177

After the speeches, student representative Liu Liangzhan gave a response speech, saying that I would like to represent all the students who are going abroad and express our sincere gratitude to the gentlemen who have come to the meeting. Listening to your teachings has been of great benefit and inspiration. I also feel that the mission is heavy and I am as if standing on the edge of a deep abyss. However, I will be able to understand the meaning of the elders' encouragement and dare not be idle or negligent, so as not to disappoint your high hopes. As for the achievements of students who have studied abroad, there are sometimes bad ones. This is a personal problem for the students themselves and is not a problem with the study abroad system itself. Among those who are going abroad this time, there are many wealthy people, but there are also many poor people. I dare to believe that those who are going abroad this time will be able to compete with each other and do their best to learn more about China's lack of knowledge, discuss more books that are not easily seen in China, and do more construction work that China urgently needs, so that we can be of benefit to China in any way possible.

Final Entertainment 178

After the speeches from all walks of life, tea and snacks were served. Finally, for entertainment, Miss Shen Yuanyu, a talented student from the Shanghai Art College and daughter of Mr. Shen Erchang, was specially invited to sing a Peking opera piece, "The Goddess Scattering Flowers," which was round and jade-like, melodious and pleasing to the ear. Then, at the request of the students, Municipal Chamber of Commerce Chairman Wang Xiaolai also sang a piece, "Eight Hundred and Eighty Years," which was firm and powerful, with a rich and mellow flavor, adding a lot of color to the meeting. It was not until 7:00 PM that everyone dispersed joyfully.

The Far Eastern Games Next Year Will Cancel the Overall Championship 185

—The Conference Will Be Postponed to June 9th to 17th—

—The Proposal to Hire Neutral Countries as Referees Was Not Approved—

(Manila News) The Board of Directors of the Philippine Amateur Athletic Association held its annual meeting on July 28th. In addition to re-electing the directors of the association, there were several important resolutions regarding the Far Eastern Games next year, as follows:

Cancellation of the Overall Championship 186

Regarding the Japanese proposal to cancel the overall championship of the Far Eastern Games, it was agreed that each sport competition should have a championship, like the International Olympic Games.

Postponement of the Conference Date 187

Regarding the Japanese proposal to postpone the date of the Far Eastern Games next year, it was resolved to change the date from May 12th to 19th to June 9th to 17th.

Neutral Referees 188

Regarding the Japanese proposal to hire neutral referees for the Far Eastern Games next year, such as having Chinese referees for matches between Japan and the Philippines, this proposal was not agreed upon. The Board of Directors believes that the established custom of the Far Eastern Games is that the host country has the right to choose officials and referees when the games are held in that country, so there is no reason to change it at present. However, the Board of Directors resolved to accommodate as many officials and referees from participating countries as possible in the next year's games. (July 29th)

National Games Registration Begins

Deadline is September 25th 189

Water and Transportation Issues at the Venue Are Being Prepared

The National Games are approaching. Since the Organizing Committee took over the venue, the General Affairs Group has moved to the Central Stadium to work. The venue has already begun to be repaired, but because the building has been around for two years, the collapsed ground has been soaked by rainwater, making it uneven, so the repair work is quite time-consuming. The issues of funding, transportation, and water for the Games have been completely resolved. The Organizing Committee held group meetings overnight to discuss registration, tickets, and the reduction of train fares by the railway department. In addition to the reduction of train fares by the railway department, which has been reported in this newspaper, the rest are reported as follows:

Ticket Prices Determined 190

For the temporary transportation of the Games, the Organizing Committee originally planned to rent 50 cars for athletes and spectators to ride. It is now learned that the committee has repeatedly discussed this and decided to add 20 more cars because 50 cars are not enough. They are currently in negotiations with the highway bureaus of various provinces and cities. It is estimated that each car can carry 30 people, rotating between the First Plaza of Nanjing Xin Jiekou and the Central Stadium. As for the ticket price for spectators, it has been decided to sell each ticket for 2 jiao. Volunteers and staff will be assigned a number of cars for special transportation, free of charge. There are no restrictions on private vehicles. Ticket sales for spectators will be from October 10th to 20th, and for athletes and staff from October 5th to 22nd or 23rd. The wages for drivers and gasoline will be provided by the Games, estimated to cost more than 35,000 yuan. In order to welcome spectators to visit the venue, the price of admission tickets has been decided to be 1 jiao each, according to the practice of the 20th National Games.

Water for the Venue Has Also Been Resolved 191

When the venue was taken over, the members of the Organizing Committee inspected the site and found that the water problem was the most difficult. There were only five artesian wells in Dongchang, and according to the calculation of 30 gallons of water needed per day, the amount of water was far from enough. After several discussions, it was decided to ask the Department of Health to test the water in the Erdao Ditch pond in front of the Mausoleum. If it was drinkable, it would be taken. The test results showed that it could be used as long as it was disinfected. Therefore, it was decided to connect water pipes from the pond to the venue and draw water from the artesian wells to the pond. After disinfection, it would be poured into the swimming pool for storage. Sand filters would also be set up to filter the disinfected water and inject it into the reservoir for use. However, the reservoir is very small, so it is planned to set up another 200 water tanks for adjustment. As for the water fee, it has been decided to pay 1 yuan per 1,000 gallons, and it is estimated that 5,000 yuan will be paid to the Mausoleum Management Committee for water fees during the Games.

Sending Letters to Provinces and Cities to Register 192

The competition rules have been drafted by each group and are being reviewed by the committee. Regarding the registration date for athletes from various provinces and cities, the committee has not set a uniform date due to the different distances. Once the rules have been reviewed, they will be sent to the education bureaus of each province and city along with the registration form. Registration must be completed by September 25th. After September 25th, athletes from all over the country can set off for Beijing. Regarding the accommodation of the athletes, in addition to the dormitories built in the Central Stadium for the athletes, in order to facilitate the dietary habits of the athletes from all over the country, the committee has hired cooks to be contracted directly by the athletes. The dietary expenses will be borne by the provinces and cities themselves. According to Kang Youyi, the funds raised by various provinces and cities for the Games will be allocated to the athletes' meals.

Appropriately Increase Funding for the Games 193

(Beijing, 13th) Wang Shijie and Zhu Minyi have contacted Wang several times to request that he find a way to meet the approved budget according to Jiang’s reply. Wang has agreed to appropriately increase the funding. The committee has been reviewing the budgets of various groups in recent days to determine the final budget. In addition to the revenue from tickets, estimated at more than 20,000 yuan, at least 90,000 yuan is needed. In order to save money, they are trying to reduce the expenses wherever possible.

Tianjin Suffers Complete Defeat in the Inter-Port Tennis Match 194

Shanghai Wins 5-0

The third day of the Shanghai-Tianjin Inter-Port Tennis Tournament was held yesterday at the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce. There were two or three hundred spectators. There was one group each for singles and doubles, and Shanghai won all the matches again. In singles, Machida (Shanghai) defeated Faber (Tianjin), 6-3, 4-6, 6-4, 7-5. In doubles, Qiu Feihai and Jiang Daozhang (Shanghai) defeated Lun Qiang and Jie Hansheng (Tianjin), 6-1, 6-4, 6-2. In total, Shanghai won all five matches. The Tianjin players were of average strength, resulting in a complete defeat. The Tianjin team only won three sets in the five matches.

A group photo of the players and staff of the Shanghai and Tianjin Inter-Port Tennis Teams (Zheng Zhaojia was not included in the photo) (Photo by Xu Tianzhang)

Yesterday's Singles Match 195

Shanghai had already won the championship with a score of 3-0 in the first two days of the competition, so the outcome of yesterday's match had no impact on the championship. The singles match between Machida and Faber started at 3 pm. The two players were evenly matched. In the usual situation, Machida defeated Faber 3-1.

First Set 196

Machida started with an advantage, leading 3-1. Faber attacked the baseline and took Machida's serve. Afterwards, Faber attacked the net many times, but Machida also broke through with baseline shots, making it 5-2. After each adding one game, Machida ended the first set with a score of 6-3.

Second Set 197

Machida was forced to lose two games, but Machida won the next three games in a row. Faber seemed tired. Unexpectedly, Faber also added three games in a short time, taking the lead with a score of 5-3. Faber served to win the tenth game, making it 6-4. Faber won.

Third Set 198

Machida's balls went out of bounds many times, and Faber won two consecutive "smooth fours". Then he won three consecutive games, almost the same as the second set. However, Faber lost one game after winning the sixth game. Machida lost the eighth game on serve. Afterwards, Machida's courage increased greatly, and his shots became fierce, changing his gentle state, and he won again with a score of 6-4.

Fourth Set 199

Machida created an equal endgame in a winning situation, but finally won 7-5. When Machida led 4-2, Faber served in the seventh game and lost 15-40 (1-3), but he was still able to turn the tide and win a game. Machida fought to win the eighth game, taking a 5-3 lead, but in two games, Machida had gains and losses, and was finally won by Faber in a row, making it 5-5. Machida launched another fierce attack, making Faber unable to return, and took the lead again with a game. The next game became a smooth four, and Machida ended with a score of 7-5.

Yesterday's Doubles Match 200

After the singles match, the final doubles match began immediately. It was already past five o'clock. Shanghai's Qiu Feihai and Jiang Daozhang defeated Lun Qiang and Jie Hansheng in straight sets, which was very easy.

First Set 201

Lun Qiang served first. Without fierce fighting, he lost a game. Qiu Feihai attacked the boundary near the net, making his opponents sigh helplessly, unable to grip the ball. Jiang Daozhang's net interception had both merits and demerits. The game was not tense. Qiu Wang won the first five games and won the first set with a score of 6-1.

Second Set 202

If the first set was in the initial test period, the situation in the second set was slightly tense. Both sides used close combat, and the performance gradually became exciting. After Shanghai won the first game, Tianjin returned two games, but then Shanghai won four consecutive games, and victory with a score of 5-2 was again in the hands of Qiu Jiang. Although the opponents won two games, they finally lost again with a score of 4-6.

Third Set 203

Shanghai won first, Tianjin quickly won a game. After Qiu Feihai served to win the third game, in the fourth game, the two sides entered a melee of close combat. The back and forth of one ball was more than ten times, and all were rescued with difficulty. The spectators applauded a lot. However, the Tianjin team only had the ability to parry and no ability to counterattack. Shanghai took the lead again with a score of 5-1, and then each added a game to end.

The Success Stories of Two Tennis Players Published 211

(1) Lin Baohua's Success Story

(2) Qiu Feihai's Success Story

Lin Baohua and Qiu Feihai, two famous tennis players in our country, have excellent skills and are known internationally. In general, athletes and tennis enthusiasts are not impressed and admire Lin and Qiu. But Lin and Qiu have a unique experience in achieving success in tennis, which is what those who admire them must explore. Now, the Diligence Bookstore at No. 392 Labor Father Road in the French Concession of this port has specially commissioned Mr. Jiang Huaiqing, a reporter from Shen Bao Tiyu, to compile two books: "Lin Baohua's Tennis Success Story" and "Qiu Feihai's Tennis Success Story," which are published today. The two books describe in detail the origin of Lin and Qiu's success in tennis and the characteristics of their skills, and include many valuable photos of the two performing their skills and postures. The contents of the two books are detailed as follows: (1) Lin Baohua's Tennis Success Story, Chapter 1 Introduction, Chapter 2 Family Life, Chapter 3 The Beginning of Playing Tennis, Chapter 4 The Time of Fame, Chapter 5 English, Chapter 6 The 8th Far Eastern Games, Chapter 7 Davis Cup, Chapter 8 Michigan State Championship, Chapter 9 New Jersey State Championship, Chapter 10 Runner-up of the Western United States Tennis Tournament, Chapter 11 Runner-up of the Misha State, Chapter 12 Defeat of the Honolulu Championship, Chapter 13 Carnival, Chapter 14 National Zonal Tennis Tournament, Chapter 15 The New Era of Shanghai Tennis, Chapter 16 Results of the Inter-Port Tournament, Chapter 17 Final Words. (2) Qiu Feihai's Tennis Success Story, Chapter 1 Mr. Qiu's Experience, Chapter 2 Skills and Temperament, Chapter 3 Showing up in Huiboer, Chapter 4 Achievements in the Far Eastern Games, Chapter 5 Engaging with World Famous Players, Chapter 6 Three Battles with Lin Baohua, Chapter 7 Honors of the Shanghai International Championship, Chapter 8 Most Glorious Achievements, Chapter 9 Mr. Qiu's Autobiography, Chapter 10 The Future of Chinese Tennis. Reading these two works not only makes the achievements of Lin and Qiu clear, but also makes it easier to improve one's own skills. The two books are luxuriously bound and priced at 3 jiao for each friend, with a 10% discount for mail orders with postage added. The bookstore's storefront at No. 554 Sima Road is also on sale.

Wireless Electricity Weekly

A Discussion of Jiao Yitang's Letter to the Nation Regarding the Adoption of National Medicine Regulations (Continued) 214

— Yu Yunxiu

Mr. Jiao says, "From the perspective of us third parties, Western medicine has its strengths and weaknesses, and national medicine has its weaknesses and strengths." Mr. Jiao, as the head of the National Medicine Hall, suddenly wants to speak from a third-party position, claiming to have an objective perspective. I'm afraid that's not right. I believe that there isn't a single thing in the world that is completely harmful or completely useless. As the saying goes, "Every advantage has a disadvantage." For example, poison can cure diseases, licorice can harmonize, and dog excrement and sparrow droppings can soften leather. Even disease-causing microorganisms can be used to treat severe illnesses. A type of deformed syphilis in the nervous system, called "general paresis," is now known to be treatable with malaria parasites. Therefore, something considered harmful and useless from one perspective may be beneficial when viewed from another. However, the two effects, benefit and harm, cannot coexist. Benefits and harms vary in magnitude, and selection is required. The ancients said it well, "Choose the greater benefit and the lesser harm." They also said, "Even small skills have their merits, but excessive pursuit leads to stagnation, so a gentleman does not engage in them." Therefore, the principle of being a person is to understand distinctions, recognize the importance of things, and then have the ability to make choices and decisions, so that one can move towards the goal without going backward. Otherwise, listening to the arguments of both sides, each with their own reasons, one cannot make a judgment and wanders aimlessly, resulting in the tragic outcome of "hesitation leads to failure, and straying leads to nowhere." Such a person is called a mediocre person; if they become a doctor, they are called a quack; if they become an official, they are called a mediocre official in the era of gentlemen, but now they can only be called a useless bureaucrat. Mediocre people cause trouble, quack doctors kill people, and useless bureaucrats ruin the country!

Mr. Jiao says, "The strengths of Western medicine lie in the progress of material civilization, the use of excellent equipment, precise diagnosis, and strict disinfection." The strengths of Western medicine are indeed limited to these few, but these strengths are acknowledged by Mr. Jiao. It can also be inferred that "national medicine lacks the progress of material civilization, lacks the use of excellent equipment, lacks precise diagnosis, and lacks strict disinfection." Mr. Jiao certainly cannot deny these shortcomings of national medicine. I believe that these strengths and weaknesses can determine the fate of medicine and are already of great significance. Mr. Jiao! Fellow countrymen! Please use a calm mind and a fair heart to listen to what I have to say. Firstly, material civilization: the object of medicine is the human body. Humans are a type of object in nature. Their sight, hearing, speech, actions, perception, thought, emotion, and various life phenomena all have definite structures and rules. At a minimum, doctors should understand human anatomy and physiology before further exploring the truth of diseases and determining treatment plans. If this basic knowledge is not yet possessed, wanting to organize various theories and study advanced topics is too far off. How can these doctors without a solid foundation truthfully treat diseases? Therefore, following Mr. Jiao's command to "explore from a theoretical perspective," the claims of national medicine to have cured certain diseases, aside from the large part that is exaggerated propaganda, are all within the scope of the four words "fortunate coincidence" mentioned in Zhang Huang's books. As the saying goes, "If the skin is gone, where will the hair attach?" What theories and techniques can be discussed? It's all false!

Secondly, the use of equipment: In simple terms, the invention of microorganisms was only possible with the microscope. Advances in abdominal surgery, allowing for direct observation of living organs, were only possible with anesthesia. Accurate diagnosis of internal problems and treatment of several malignant and stubborn tumors and skin diseases were only possible with X-rays. The excellence of equipment has a great relationship with the progress of medicine as a whole. Mr. Jiao should remember the two maxims "A craftsman who wants to do his job well must first sharpen his tools" and also that in our country, doctors have been called "craftsmen" since ancient times, with the terms "superior craftsman" and "inferior craftsman." If the equipment is not excellent, then the medical craftsman cannot do his job well. Therefore, the inability of national medicine to do its job well is an undeniable fact. In other words, the inadequacy of national medicine techniques is an inescapable causal relationship and an unshakeable conclusion.

Thirdly, precise diagnosis: Doctors should naturally diagnose accurately to prescribe medication accurately. Mr. Jiao has already acknowledged that national medicine lacks precise diagnosis. However, this matter is a major key to theory and practice in medicine, not only affecting the individual who is sick. Accurate diagnosis allows for recognition of the true nature of the disease, allowing one to apply theory to deal with it. If the disease is misidentified, it will lead to a great deviation. For example, mistaking a stroke for phlegm and desperately treating it with phlegm-removing medication. If it happens to get better, people who don't understand theory will say that the disease was indeed phlegm, and that the medication was accurate, resulting in good results. In fact, from a theoretical perspective, a stroke is certainly not phlegm but a cerebral hemorrhage. Using phlegm-removing methods to treat a cerebral hemorrhage is obviously irrelevant, and using phlegm medication to treat a cerebral hemorrhage is obviously the wrong medicine. Moreover, whether their so-called phlegm-removing medication actually removes phlegm is also completely without basis. In short, it's all nonsense fabricated out of thin air. They insist that a stroke is phlegm, insist that the treatment method is for phlegm, and insist that the medication used is phlegm medication. When the disease slightly improves, they insist that it is their technique. I remember that Lu Wenshu of the Han Dynasty wrote a memorial to the emperor advocating leniency in punishment. The most poignant part of it said: "People naturally enjoy life when they are at peace and think of death when they are in pain. Under torture, they cannot obtain what they seek. Therefore, prisoners who cannot bear the pain will embellish their words to please the interrogators. Officials who benefit from this will guide them to clarify the details. Afraid of rejection from the emperor, they will forge evidence to perfect the case. Once the case is successfully framed, even if Gao Yao hears it, he would still think that the death penalty is insufficient punishment. Why? Because many people are involved in forging the evidence, and the charges are clearly presented." Aren't national doctors forging diseases and embellishing treatments in the same way? Therefore, the Mountain and Sea Classic and the Book of Burial say: "If mountains and rivers could speak, grave diggers would have nothing to eat. If internal organs could speak, doctors would be pale with fear." Relying on the fact that internal organs cannot speak, national doctors forcibly connect pulse diagnosis, disease causes, symptom analysis, and treatment into one, to spread falsehoods and deceive the public, perpetuating errors from ancient times to the present. They not only lack the understanding of the principles for recognizing the true nature of diseases, but they also lack this kind of thinking. Therefore, because they cannot recognize the true nature of diseases, they also cannot judge whether the treatment techniques are correct or reasonable. They also cannot verify the actual effects of the medication. It all becomes a rigid situation, empty and without any practical effort, so our national medicine will never progress. This is the harmful consequence of inaccurate diagnosis for the development of medicine itself. (To be continued)

Common Knowledge of Diseases Q&A (Continued) 215

— Cheng Hanzhang

Q: What other symptoms are there?

A: There is loss of appetite, thirst, occasional vomiting or hiccups, decreased urine output, a positive double test in the urine, sometimes a positive Le Yang reaction, and redness and inflammation in the anal area, also rectal prolapse or anal relaxation.

Q: What is the course of bacterial dysentery?

A: Most cases heal in one to three weeks. However, severe cases can develop severe toxic symptoms, including high fever, collapse-like body temperature, subcutaneous bleeding, confusion, and incontinence, leading to death within a few days. In addition, some cases can become chronic.

Q: What are the complications of bacterial dysentery?

A: Complications include meteorism and dysenteric appendicitis.
