A Bird's-Eye View of Medicine and Pharmaceuticals in Shanghai in the Last Decade (Continued) 216

— Pang Jingzhou

Chapter Five: Administration of Medicine and Pharmaceuticals

Section Three: Recent Government Orders

Regarding foreign drug merchants, although the Ministry of Health has ordered them to register their products, how many have complied with the order to this day? Aren't inferior foreign drugs still being sold freely? Moreover, what can be done when Koreans naturalize as Chinese citizens, hang up American business signs, and sell German drugs? Although the regulations on the management of narcotics are being revised, they cannot be implemented smoothly. Customs only searches for them as contraband, and pharmacies sell these goods on the market. This is because there is no thorough solution. So it seems laughable. (As for the Tianjin Health Bureau, it even banned the sale of lactose in order to crack down on the so-called "white flour" poison – saying that lactose is a necessary ingredient for making white flour. Such a foot-binding government order is even more ridiculous.)

The above-mentioned government orders are mostly national affairs, but Shanghai is most deeply affected by them. As for the winter of the seventeenth year, it was precisely the era when the Ministry of Health had not yet been established, and health bureaus or public security bureaus in various regions each governed themselves. The Shanghai Medical Association once requested the authorities to postpone registration until the Medical Practitioners Law was promulgated. However, there was no way to remedy it at the time. Various places had already started one after another. Shanghai was particularly fragmented due to the concession relationship, and registration was not comprehensive. Soon, the Ministry of Health canceled the validity of registration in various places and uniformly changed to ministry registration. Not everyone necessarily obtained ministry licenses. Those who acted as overseas Chinese-style doctors only began to obtain concession licenses after being cracked down on by the French Concession and the Public Concession in December of the nineteenth year and May of the twentieth year. However, the orders were not consistent, which naturally led to the malpractice of obtaining concession licenses that did not comply with the ministry's regulations. Moreover, although the concessions have regulations for cracking down, it is difficult to implement the procedures for cracking down. How often have concession police intervened in the business of doctors? Therefore, when the ministry ordered everyone to obtain ministry licenses in the eighteenth year, someone requested the health bureau to crack down on unlicensed doctors. As a result, they only received a written reply to handle it accordingly. And last year, someone wanted to ask the concession authorities to crack down on those unlicensed quacks who misled the public with exaggerations. The concession authorities actually replied that there was no provision in Chinese law stating, "Who is allowed to practice medicine? Who is not allowed to practice medicine?" Since the courts could not easily intervene, how could the police power be enforced? In this light, the Executive Yuan's insistence on strict qualifications for doctors was merely a pretentious aristocratic claim. The medical and pharmaceutical concepts of the public were very thin.

In the winter of the seventeenth year, the Shanghai Health Bureau also issued a government order stating, "Chinese medicine practitioners shall not use Western medicine, and Western medicine practitioners shall not use Chinese medicine," forcibly conflating medicine and pharmaceuticals and leaving academic theory behind. The Health Bureau probably thought it was a clever way to prevent business disputes. (The central authorities have some people who accuse modern medicine of rejecting old medicine and old medicine of criticizing new medicine as business disputes, but we modern medicine have never admitted it.) They considered themselves as impartial and appropriate as Chen Ping dividing meat. Or perhaps it was a passive policy to prevent old medicine from misusing blood serums and other products. However, the promulgation of this order provoked criticism from the modern medicine community and resentment from those in old medicine who wanted to innovate. Another government order was that the Health Bureau, acting on the advice of the party department, wanted to limit the consultation fees of private practitioners in the city. In reality, the consultation fees of private practitioners are secretly judged by the natural forces of society. If the price is high and the skill is poor, they will inevitably be eliminated. As for the poor and sick, even consultation fees of fifty cents to one dollar are still unaffordable. How can the government order private practitioners to provide free consultations when it does not run hospitals? Therefore, this order was also a dead letter.

Recently, the Shanghai Medical Association voluntarily solicited more than fifty members to provide free consultations for one hour in different districts every day. Consultation vouchers were printed and could be obtained from the association. This can be considered a small obligation of the association to society. In summary, past medical and pharmaceutical government orders have been sometimes strict and sometimes lenient, sometimes able to be implemented and sometimes unable to be implemented but forcefully attempted, leading to a hectic and chaotic situation. This is all due to (A) a portion of the health authorities recognizing the idealized high standards of pure European and American systems; (B) a few central committee members favoring old medicine based on personal feelings and individual beliefs; (C) instigation by party departments or business associations; (D) obstruction by foreigners in the concessions. These various reasons have created many gaps that can be exploited during the repeated changes in these attempted government orders. Therefore, in this era of economic depression and declining people's livelihood, a large number of speculators have infiltrated the medical and pharmaceutical industries. This is what Wang Qizhang called "unjustified desires and opportunistic gains." I still remember when the second chapter of this article was published, I said that the Western Medicine Association was forced out by laws and regulations and that the association had no restrictions, making it easy for mixed elements to enter – which caused quite a stir among the Western Medicine Association. Now that I have clarified the facts, the Western Medicine Association can probably understand that this phenomenon does indeed hinder the overall development of modern medicine. (This is what a member of the Western Medicine Association told me.) And it will not be a misunderstanding that I have any intention of slandering it. (End of this chapter)

Several Important Discoveries and Inventions in the Process of New Medicine Development (7) 217

— Gu Shoubai

(V) Organotherapy and Secretion Theory

Humans have believed since ancient times that certain organs in the body have certain functions. This belief is not limited to primitive peoples. Even ancient and modern civilized peoples have not been without it, because they believed that courage was related to the heart. Therefore, warriors of savage tribes believed that eating the hearts of enemies could increase their courage. From this psychology, it is easy to infer that eating animal livers is effective for human liver diseases. In the writings of Celsus and Dioscorides, we find that they advocated using various animal organs to treat diseases of these organs in humans. For example, because foxes can run long distances at high speeds, they believed that fox lungs could be effective for shortness of breath. Similarly, they believed that rabbit brain could treat tremors and calf stomach could treat stomach diseases. This method continued until relatively recent times. However, in the early nineteenth century, these drugs were almost not included in pharmacopoeias. Later, after our knowledge of gastric physiology improved, we were actually able to extract gastrin from pig stomachs and make artificial gastric juice, which was used for indigestion.

Similar preparations have also been made from the pancreas. This pancreatic juice is also widely used for several indigestion conditions and has even been used to pre-digest food. This pancreatic juice is usually taken from the pancreas of pigs. Part of the food has been digested by the action of pancreatic juice, so people with stomach diseases can eat this food that has been treated with pancreatic juice without overloading their digestive system. Milk can usually be treated in this way. To explain in detail, it is to add some artificial pancreatic juice to a certain amount of milk, store the mixed liquid at the same temperature as body temperature, and after a certain period of time, allow the enzymes in the pancreatic juice to act on the components of the milk, just like the action of pancreatic juice on milk in the human body, and then use it as a drink. This method does have value, but it also has limitations. Usually, it should not be pre-digested for too long, otherwise this food may inevitably lose its deliciousness and will not be enough to be eaten. The principles of the above-mentioned application of gastric juice and pancreatic juice are relatively simple. In addition, we have more complicated methods for applying organs to treat diseases, which are specially called organotherapy.

Most of the secretions of the glandular organs in the body are mostly injected into the body cavity through ducts to manage various beneficial effects. For example, the secretion of the salivary glands often assists the digestion of food in the oral cavity.

However, the secretions of some glandular organs are not injected into the body cavity through ducts, but directly enter the circulatory system through lymphatic vessels or blood vessels and circulate throughout the body to manage various special effects. This secretion is particularly called endocrine secretion, which is very important in modern medicine. According to recent research, it is known that some diseases are caused by the deficiency or changes of certain endocrine organs. The first endocrine organ discovered was the thyroid gland in front of the neck.

Random Notes After Diagnosis 218

— Chen Fangzhi

Introduction in lieu of a preface

I am a doctor, and diagnosing illnesses is my duty. I should focus on my work and fulfill my duties, so why should I write this random notes? But you must know that we are in a transitional era in China, and all social phenomena are in contradictions and abnormalities, and medical affairs cannot escape this general rule. You must know that practicing medicine in a foreign society only requires doctors to do their best, use their keen eyes and wisdom to diagnose disease symptoms; apply their broad knowledge and medical rules; and they can fulfill their duties. But in Chinese society, the contradictions and abnormalities of medical affairs are encountered almost every day. When we encounter these contradictions and abnormalities, sometimes a strange feeling of oppression and uprightness arises in our chest, and we cannot help but release it. Sometimes infinite pity and sorrow are reflected in our eyes, and we cannot help but give advice. Sometimes, we even hold back the humorous nature in our noses and cannot help but play with a blunt pen to relieve the fatigue of our work. This is the origin of "Random Notes After Diagnosis."

On the Shanghai Bund, in the concession area, after all, it is the source of international cooperation. Two or three years ago, I went with a few friends to Wusong to breathe the fresh air by the sea. We heard two people pointing and gesturing in front of a large house, saying, "What is this strange place? On the one hand, it hangs the signboard of the Chinese National Medical College, and on the other hand, it hangs the signboard of the kerosene king." "What is that? The government of the Republic of China, in the Republic of China, runs the National University of the Republic of China, and it has to rely on foreigners to donate a piece of land to build a school base. Do you understand this contradictory fact?" "I understand. Because if you want the children of China to learn the medicine of universal harmony, you must first have them learn the example of international cooperation." Now I look at the Japanese, who hung up the signboard of Manchukuo in the three eastern provinces and want the Manchus to be puppets, pulling the strings behind them. It turns out that they have guessed the spirit of international cooperation and universal harmony of our noble countrymen. They say that I run the South Manchuria Medical College to educate Chinese children and that I run the Dalian Medical Staff to rescue Chinese coolies. Long live international cooperation! Long live universal harmony! Once, at a friend's house, I heard a Mr. Wang say, "There is a wealthy man with five or sixty thousand strings of cash at home. He suffered a mild stroke, and his right hand and right foot were not moving well. He asked a foreign doctor from a certain sanatorium to see him, and the doctor said that his blood pressure was too high and that he should have a bloodletting. After agreeing on a bloodletting fee of five hundred taels, he asked the doctor to carry it out. Unexpectedly, too much blood was let out. At first, his face turned pale, then he twitched, and finally, he died. The foreign doctor still said some sarcastic remarks, saying, "It doesn't matter, it doesn't matter, put him on the soil, and he will be fine if he is not given anything to eat for two days and nights." One asked Mr. Wang in surprise, "How much blood was let out in the end?" He said, "About three or four pounds." I said, "He should have died. The amount of blood in a person is about one-twelfth or one-thirteenth of their body weight. Acute blood loss of more than one-fifth is life-threatening. Assuming that the wealthy man weighed one hundred and twenty or thirty pounds, his blood volume would be about ten pounds. Letting out three or four pounds would be fatal!" I also asked him how much the bloodletting fee was. He said that five hundred taels were paid. Originally, Chinese people living in the concession area, even if they were injured, would only obediently pay the injury fee to foreigners. We often hear that the appendicitis surgery fee in a certain foreign hospital is one thousand taels, the X-ray fee is seven hundred taels, and the radium treatment fee is two thousand taels. We also often hear people who pay the money say that the foreign hospital is really good and clean, and it should be expensive. We also often hear people say that medical expenses are really expensive now, four cents for a prescription of winter frost leaves and summer bitter herbs, and two yuan for a consultation with Dr. Zhao or Dr. Qian. Comparing these two statements,

You must know that people with the root of universal harmony, who live in the concession area, should believe in foreign goods. What is so strange about that! (To be continued)

Free Talk

Talking About Sequels 219

— Qifan

It is said that there are as many as seven or eight types of sequels to Dream of the Red Chamber, but none of them are worth reading. The ancient saying "to add a dog's tail to a sable coat" is indeed something to sigh about.

Sequels are not easy to write. A complete work must already have formed a world of its own, with a unique and complete system. To write a sequel, one must first understand everything in that world in the original work and see the inevitable development and trends that will be produced, and then unfold a new situation based on this. In this way, the sequel and the original can be connected and become a real sequel. Writing randomly without understanding it is nonsense.

So sequels are very difficult to write, at least no easier than original works that break new ground, but there are many people who write sequels without knowing this difficulty. For every small famous work that can be profitable, there are always more than one person writing a sequel. They are not writing sequels, but using the name to make a profit. Their purpose is only to borrow the already famous book title to make it easier to appeal and make money. These kinds of sequels should be overthrown.

There are also people who genuinely write sequels, either continuing the unfinished work of a friend or because they have been greatly moved by reading a work and feel that they must express themselves, but very few people do well. Because before the sequel, there is already an established and complete world, and everything must start from there. It is definitely not the same as writing chapter novels, continuing chapter after chapter. Therefore, if you take the attitude of writing a chapter novel to write a sequel, you will definitely fail. Therefore, a work that is very good when read as a chapter novel, for example, with rich content, many twists and turns in the situation, beautiful words, and truly moving writing, becomes a good work in itself, but if it is a sequel to a certain book instead of starting from scratch, it may not be good when viewed as a sequel, because sequels have other main points, as mentioned above.

It is difficult to write sequels to novels, and we can always forgive if they are not written well, but those that are very clever when not seen as sequels but become unrecognizable when seen as sequels are really a bit funny.

The Uselessness of Pessimism 220

— A Traveler from隼

Among elegant scholars, there are indeed some who are particularly adept at shedding tears. They say that because of the chaos in the Chinese literary scene in recent years, it's like warlords carving up territory, and they can't help but cry "Alas!" But especially lament the slander.

In reality, the era of writing to be "stored in famous mountains" is gone, and once there's a "literary scene," there's bound to be struggle, even to the point of insults and slander. The late Ming Dynasty is too far away, so let's not mention it; in the Qing Dynasty, Zhang Shizhai and Yuan Zicai, Li Yuchun and Zhao Huishu were as incompatible as fire and water. Closer to our time, the disputes between "Min Bao" and "Xinmin Congbao," and between the "New Youth" faction and some other faction, were also extremely fierce. In the beginning, didn't they also make outsiders shake their heads and sigh? However, once the victor is clear and the era recedes into the distance, the blood of battle is washed clean by the rain, and later generations believe that the literary scene of the past was peaceful. It's the same in foreign countries. We now mostly only know that Ibsen and Hauptmann were outstanding literary figures, but when their works were first performed, people were arrested and fought in the theaters. Detailed literary histories even record illustrations of such fights.

Therefore, whether in China or abroad, ancient or modern, the literary scene is always chaotic, making elegant scholars "pessimistic." But in the end, many so-called literary figures and writings will certainly perish, and only those that deserve to exist will ultimately survive, proving that the literary scene is still a clean place. What adds to the chaos are some pessimists who, without investigation or criticism, use the argument that "that is also a right and wrong, this is also a right and wrong" to denigrate all authors as "birds of a feather." In this way, the chaos will never end. However, the world is not all like that; there will certainly be clear distinctions between right and wrong. Let us think about it: Lin Qinnan's attacks on the novels of the literary revolution didn't last long. Where are they now?

Only the recent slander seems to be a rather outstanding trick, but in reality, it is not more severe than in ancient times. The evidence is the anecdotes of the literary inquisition in the early Qing Dynasty. Moreover, those who engage in such tricks are not entirely literary figures. Nine out of ten are just hanging up a signboard without any goods to sell, and can only turn into a dark shop, selling human meat buns like petty thieves. Even if there are occasionally people who have once dabbled in writing, at this time they are precisely revealing their true colors, confessing their own decline. The literary scene will not be confused by this; on the contrary, it will become clearer and more distinct.

History never regresses, and there is no need to be pessimistic about the literary scene. Pessimism arises from standing outside the situation, not distinguishing right from wrong, and yet insisting on caring about the literary scene, or perhaps from sitting in a declining camp oneself.

Further Discussion on Kong Yiji 221

— Zizhan

My previous work, "Kong Yiji," was included in the 　庐絮语. I said that this method of tracing red characters existed before the Tang and Song dynasties. Recently, I received from Mr. Ruozhang a copy of his book, "A Superficial Investigation of the Origins of Vulgar Customs," containing the entry "Shang Da Ren," which further proves that my previous statement was not a mistake. The summary is as follows: Liang Zhangju's "Sequel to Rambling Talks" quotes the "Transmission of the Lamp" as saying, "Someone asked Venerable Chen, 'What is the teaching of an era?' Chen said, 'Shang da ren, qiu yi yi.'" The "Wudeng Huiyuan" records that Guo Gongfu visited Baiyun, who said, "Last night I composed a eulogy to the mountains on my pillow to thank the great Confucian Guo Gongfu, namely, 'Shang da ren, qiu yi yi, hua san qian, qi shi shi. Er xiao sheng, ba jiu zi, jia zuo ren, ke zhi li ye.'" Gongfu initially doubted, but later heard a child reciting it and understood. According to this, the phrase already existed in the Tang and Song dynasties. Zhu Zhishan's "Vulgar Talks" explains its meaning as, "This is Kongzi's letter to his father. 'Shang da ren' is one sentence. 'Kong' is one sentence, meaning Kongzi referring to himself. 'Yi yi hua san qian qi shi shi er' is one sentence, saying that the scholar he has transformed into is of such a number. 'Xiao sheng ba jiu zi jia' is one sentence, 'ba jiu' meaning seventy-two, saying that among the three thousand people, seventy-two are even better. 'Zuo ren ke zhi li' is another sentence, 'zuo' meaning 'is,' benevolence and propriety being used together, seventy characters doing good is benevolence, its propriety is knowable." I do not know what the life of teachers in the Tang and Song dynasties was like. However, judging from this primer for beginners, it can be seen that their learning was simple and crude, not far from the Kong Yiji described by Mr. Lu Xun. In the popular dramas performed by farmers in my hometown, there is a type called Zhang Hutu, one topic being "Mr. Zhang Demands School Fees." This also describes the clumsy literati of the old era. Zhang Hutu is also of the Kong Yiji type. Zhang Hutu describes his teacher life as follows:

First, I bid farewell to Confucius, and on both sides, I bid farewell to the worthy men. Teaching is a difficult thing, the most worthless of people, the stinking scholar. Teaching is difficult, truly difficult, blue clothes sitting, white back sitting crooked. Teaching until the tenth month is full, good students will return the money. Bad students will slander, saying that the teacher is playing with the students. After reading the Four Books and Five Classics, a belly full of writing is remembered in the heart. Although I am not a reading seed, I am still teaching students with a book. In the first month, it is the New Year, every household goes to welcome the lanterns. The student invites me to watch the lanterns, afraid of disgracing my literary style. In the second month, it is the Flower Festival, the student invites me to teach at the school. He asks how much the tuition is, I say one hundred is not too much, eighty is not too little, half a liter of rice I also want.

In the third month, it is Qingming, every household goes to the ancestral tombs. The student invites me to go on an outing, pumpkin stew with meat awaits the teacher. In the fourth month, mid-fourth month, the student invites me to dinner. Wine, meat, fish, and shrimp are eaten in one meal, also sending a few salted duck eggs. In the fifth month, it is the Dragon Boat Festival, the teacher returns to his hometown. Every student sends festival tea, giving me a few old cucumbers. In the sixth month, it is the dog days, teaching makes me sweat profusely. The tuition is only sixty coins, but the teacher must teach for a year. In the seventh month, the seventh day of the seventh month, teaching has only one brush. The Five Classics and Four Books I do not know, the Three Character Classic I am the first. In the eighth month, it is the Mid-Autumn Festival, the teacher has reached the end. Every student pays their respects with the festival, each bringing a mooncake. This drama uses the mouth of the confused Mr. Zhang to write out the false elegance, poverty, and bitter life of the teacher. The tune is humorous and interesting, also giving much sympathy to those village teachers. The teachers are close to the farmers, so in the farmers' dramas, they are not completely antagonistic figures. When the National Revolutionary Army first rose, the peasant associations in various places all had elementary school teachers participating, also because elementary school teachers were closest to the farmers, both belonging to the dominated class, and their economic status was also somewhat equivalent. The era of Zhang Hutu and Kong Yiji-like teachers has long passed, today's elementary school teachers should know how to encourage themselves.

On Children's Education 222

— Yi Yun

Having worked as an elementary school teacher for over a year, I really dare not say that I have any insights into children's education. No, when I think of children, when I think of these many relatively pure people, I cannot help but feel deeply guilty. In the present day, when everything is commodified, not to mention the children who cannot enter school, even those who are fortunate enough to enter school are pitifully subjected to education that cannot be told to outsiders. The other day, I saw several teachers discussing the compilation of textbooks, but dead textbooks need living people to teach them. What actually cultivates children's character and increases their knowledge is still the elementary school teacher. How to make children automatically study, and use books to develop their understanding by drawing parallels and making inferences, completely depends on whether the teacher can become one with the children. The teacher should put all their heart and mind into the children, and should have a naive childlike heart and a sharp mind, so that the children can happily follow you without realizing it. The education of love is very, very important in elementary school. However, in today's new schools, there is no so-called corporal punishment, but the situation where students become dull and wooden as soon as they see the teacher is still everywhere. The reason is of course that the teachers are too teacher-like, punishing students by making them write repeatedly or stand in the corner at the slightest movement, so that the children cannot help but tremble at the sight of them. However, elementary school teachers have their own difficulties in being like this. Speaking of the life of an elementary school teacher, its tedium and poverty are almost universally known. A five-month contract is enough to make them worry once at the end of each semester, and the hourly wage on weekdays makes them tremble and dare not be absent, even if they are sick, they endure it and go to class. Otherwise, excluding Sundays in a month, if they take a few more sick days, they will have to tighten their belts. Elementary school teachers who are forced to sell their time and labor have no choice but to be stingy with the time that has not been sold in order to make up for the lack of livelihood. As a result, the children are perfunctorily treated. In addition to the regular lessons in the textbooks, they can no longer get much more from the teachers, because the extra energy and time that the teachers spend is unpaid, they cannot talk about education on an empty stomach, and they cannot educate other people's children while their own children have no food to eat. Because of the need to finish those textbooks by the end of the semester, they have no choice but to put pressure on the children like debt collectors. As a result, cowardly and opportunistic qualities are cultivated among the children, and "perfunctory treatment from top to bottom" has become the state of education today. For the sake of humanity, we must not let our children continue to receive that kind of incomprehensible education, but to have good education, we must have good teachers, and to have good teachers, we must first ensure that they have some security in their lives. But in the current social system, is there anyone who can devote themselves to a certain career without having to worry about their livelihood?

Ordinary Matters (38) 223

— Jun Guo Sun

"There was no discussion, because everyone didn't know to look for the old boss. He saw that there were several people in the dining hall, so he first greeted everyone generally, and then exchanged pleasantries with Botang and stated his purpose:

"Tonight's dinner, please be sure to grace us with your presence."

"Brother, you're going to so much trouble, I really don't deserve it."

"Please be sure to come to my humble abode for a visit."

"I really don't deserve it. I received your call earlier and should have replied immediately, but now that you've come to invite me in person, I'm truly very sorry..." "We're all familiar people, Brother Botang, why do you say such things! I've been trying to call more than ten times but couldn't get through, so I came in person."

"In principle, Brother Zichun, I really should obey your command, but it just so happens that there's some family business at home today, important family business, so I really can't spare the time. I can only appreciate your invitation in my heart."

Shen Bao Fifth Sheet

Economic Special Issue

Some Thoughts on the Rural Revival Problem Shishihao 224

In recent months, the revival of rural areas has been emphasized by both the government and the public. It is claimed that the country is based on agriculture and that farmers account for more than 85% of the total population, yet rural areas have been declining year by year and are on the verge of collapse. This is truly a major concern for the national economy and the people's livelihood. More than twenty types of theories and proposals have been put forward to trace the reasons for this and to plan for the future. However, the implications of economic problems are like the pyramids of Egypt. The more numerous the lowest layer, the simpler and more acute the center of gravity of the highest layer must be. Although the rural problem can be analyzed in detail, there must also be a comprehensive reason for grasping the key points. To make a comprehensive observation, one must first have the following premises. Modern economy is also called world transportation economy. The circulation of goods and finance has hardly any national boundaries to divide. Therefore, the rise and fall of prices and the level of interest rates tend to be the same all over the world. This is what is called free competition of economy. Therefore, although there are differences in the production cost of goods, the rise and fall of prices must be balanced, and no one city or industry can monopolize for a long time. This situation is most evident in the products of small production businesses. The selling price of products is almost entirely controlled by the market. The individual cost is negligible. If the scale of the business is large, the output of the product is huge. Since it has considerable control over the supply and demand of the market, it also has relatively autonomous control over the rise and fall of prices. Monopoly businesses, trust organizations, and state-run trade in Soviet Russia are all good examples of this. This is the first premise that those who observe production businesses should understand. A production business is an economic business. The principle of economics says that the greatest effect should be obtained with the least labor and expense. This is also true of production businesses. Therefore, labor and expenses must be minimized, and selling prices must be maximized. Only when labor and expenses are small can costs be light, and when costs are light, selling prices may be lower than market prices. Therefore, although selling prices are reduced, the business can still prosper day by day. Conversely, if costs are higher than those of general competitors, and the selling price of the product cannot be free from the control of the market price, then those who only cover their expenses in normal times will be profitable for their competitors; those who can still break even when prices fall will not be able to avoid losing money. Since the profits of the business are lagging behind step by step, decline and collapse are inevitable. The rise and fall of all production businesses are generally viewed in this way. This is the second premise that those who observe production businesses should understand.

The cost of a product has direct and indirect distinctions. The proportion of indirect costs allocated to products must be lower for large-scale producers than for small-scale producers. Indirect costs are especially so; such as management fees; such as marketing fees, etc., the larger the output, the more economical the allocation rate. Even extending to direct costs, large-scale use is also more economical than small-scale use. Moreover, the so-called economy here is not only the quality and quantity of use. The purchase price of materials required for various costs, the wages of labor, and the interest on silver, large-scale businesses are also more economical than small-scale businesses. The lower product costs of business organizations such as trusts, cartels, etc., are all due to this. This is the third premise that those who observe production businesses should understand.

The production of goods has the distinction between manual system and machine system. The manual system requires human labor everywhere, and human labor must have a considerable cost of living. Although productivity is smaller, the cost of human labor cannot be too low. If it is too low, it will not be enough to maintain its life, and people will abandon this work. The machine system can save human labor, often with two or three people managing a machine, and the productivity is enough to match dozens to hundreds of people. Therefore, although its production is larger, the proportion of expenses allocated to producers is smaller. Human labor expenses are originally the main part of the cost of a product. Machine production can save human labor, and its cost is naturally lower than that of the manual system. This is the fourth premise that those who observe production businesses should understand.

Judging from the above four premises, it can be seen that in the current world economic trend, only large-scale production and machine production can survive. The larger the scale of production and the more extensive the use of machines, the more economical the cost and the more applicable the economic principle. In the near future, business people can occupy an advantage in the market, and in the long run, social people's livelihood should not be difficult to benefit from. The university has a cloud, "Those who give birth are many," which is the production method that conforms to economic principles.

○○○○○

Our country's rural areas are indeed the production business of agricultural products. In this world traffic economy, since we cannot close ourselves off, we cannot but be subject to the economic principles of agriculture in various countries of the world. Now let us see how the control it receives compares with that of the general agriculture of the world?

The mass production system is a characteristic of general production organizations since the industrial revolution. Industry is no exception. Just like Nungye, it also has this tendency. The large-scale cultivation in the United States is known to everyone. Since 1929, Soviet Russia has implemented a policy of collective production in agriculture. Therefore, the amount of mineral products has made the most long-term progress. In our country, although there are large landlords, there are still many small tenant farmers. Those with cultivated land of less than ten mu almost account for half of the total number of farmers. Speaking of the size of the production organization, our country's rural areas are inherently backward.

The use of the machine system in the production business, the industry is actually the first, followed by agriculture. England, the United States, and Soviet Russia are all its authors. According to British statistics, the latest mechanized steel plow can cultivate about 25 to 40 acres per day, compared with manual labor, the speed is truly incalculable. Our country's rural areas have always relied on the manual system for their farming methods. Although livestock are used for plowing, the speed of work is not enough to look forward to the back of the machine system. Speaking of production technology, our country's rural areas are also backward.

In terms of the organization and technology of production, the production labor of our country's agricultural products is probably more than that of various countries. However, its prices cannot but be subject to the control of the world market. Large labor costs and small gains are what is feared by economic principles. Although it is said that the living standard of farmers is lower than that of various countries. However, the necessary cost of living must be sought to be maintained. This kind of living cost is also part of the cost, then the cost must not be as low as those who use machines. The fact that our country's agriculture cannot compete with various countries in the world is also due to economic principles. When the selling price is not enough to cover the cost, and the income is not enough to cover the expenses, the cash outflow of the rural areas, the equipment of agriculture is even more humble. Land prices are getting lower and lower, and wasteland is increasing day by day. The hidden treasures are getting more and more, the production is getting less and less, the refugees are getting more and more, and the bandits are becoming more and more prosperous. All the phenomena of rural misery arise one after another. Recently, it is not only declining, it is in danger of collapsing. The source of poverty is just losing money. Losing money is what is greatly feared by production businesses.

Furthermore, the high cost of our country's agricultural products is not only due to the improper production organization and technology. The heavy indirect costs are also sufficient to cause it. Such as especially heavy taxes, the exploitation of individual rents, and the heavy erosion of intermediaries in sales, none of them is not enough to increase the cost and reduce the net profit. The former is due to special reasons, and the latter two are still the malpractices caused by small production organizations. The backward production organization and production technology are truly the major reasons for the rural loss of money. According to the above-mentioned arguments, in order to revive rural areas, two major plans should be implemented in the agricultural business itself:

(1) Nationalization of land, private ownership of land, unequal distribution, and the annexation of the powerful. In densely populated areas, farmers cannot obtain their land. In sparsely populated areas, the benefits of the land cannot be fully utilized. There are many obstacles to the promotion of large production organizations. Moreover, in private ownership, landlords can sit back and eat, and tenants bear the burden of rent. The former is wasteful in terms of social economy, and the latter is to increase the indirect costs of agricultural products. Both are sufficient to hinder the proper development of people's livelihood. Therefore, it should now be taken over by the state. The state should divide the land according to the current situation of farmers. Farmers' cultivated land is not limited to the present. The wasteland in the northwest can also be used. Farmers' production organizations are not based on each household as a unit. Hundreds of thousands of households can also cultivate and live together. In short, the land should be used as a war position in the society, making it a vital land, and making it a land for large-scale production organizations. This is the meaning of nationalization of land

(2) The use of machines is enough to increase productivity, which has been commonly seen since the industrial revolution. Farming relies on the power of human and animal, it takes a long time and costs a lot of labor. It is not in line with economic principles. Large-scale use of machines is indispensable. Machines of course also have costs, and their costs must be allocated to agricultural products. However, compared with the cost of humans and animals, it must be economical. Then it can be confirmed in the manual industry and the machine-made industry. However, the more widely used machines are used for farming, the more economical the cost. Moreover, those who do not have a wide range of cultivated land and thick financial resources are not sufficient to widely use machines. Therefore, it is only applicable under large production organizations. Furthermore, large production organizations can only save costs and exert the characteristics of large production by using machines. Then, land nationalization and machine utilization have an inseparable relationship. This is the meaning of machine utilization.

If the two methods on the right can be implemented, the loss of money in agriculture will be transformed. It can at least be effective in reviving rural areas. If agriculture can be improved, the social economy will surely prosper. Then the people will be at peace and the country will be stable, and everything can be revived. Not only can taxes be reduced, but the social order can be rectified. Even natural disasters can be prevented. What is the purpose of engaging in designing trivial details in the problem of rural revival?

Moreover, the fact that large-scale production and machine production can revive rural areas is not only limited to the main industry of agricultural products. Even extending to various side industries, it is also the same. Such as handicrafts, such as animal husbandry, if they can follow this rule, the method of improvement. The cost can be reduced, and the production can also be improved. In terms of the economic principles of production businesses, large-scale production and machine production, although they also have their drawbacks, are ultimately more beneficial and less harmful. Moreover, the whole world is like this, but I alone deny it. Therefore, if we do not rush to promote it, it will not be enough to save the country.

Someone said that the area of agricultural land in our country is about 155.8 million mu, and on average, each person only gets 5 mu. If large-scale production is implemented, how will the agricultural land be insufficient for distribution? Moreover, the farmers are already in pain. If machine production is implemented to seize human labor, how will the number of unemployed farmers increase? The answer is that there is no need to worry about this. According to economic principles, the harvest of production should be sought to be more, but the workers participating in a certain production do not need to be many. The investment of labor should only be for production, and the production business is not limited to one end. Then, for the current plan, it is only necessary to use the cultivable area to engage in production with the most economical production methods. If the people have surplus labor, there are many other production businesses. It can be used to exert the production capacity of the whole people. What is the purpose of cutting off the feet to fit the shoes?

Currency and Price Charter in the Dauraixi Plan 225

In the previous article "The Most Serious Currency Issue in the Current Stage of the World Economic Panic", we roughly discussed the relationship between world currency issues and the world economic panic. Because many economists believe that the decline in prices is the fundamental reason for the downturn in all industries, and to restore world prosperity, it is necessary to artificially raise prices first; to raise prices, it is necessary to artificially devalue the currency. The current economic policy of the United States is the result of the advocacy of this type of economist. Then, regardless of whether the phenomenon of low currency value and high prices in the United States is temporary, and regardless of whether the United States can restore temporary prosperity as a result, the necessity of discussing this issue is undoubtedly clear.

I remember that when the London Conference was held, its agenda included the following six key points:

1. Restoring the gold standard; 2. Preventing the decline in prices; 3. Abolishing all means of managing exchange rates; 4. Eliminating special obstacles to international commerce, such as prohibitions and quotas; 5. Establishing an agreement to reduce and stabilize tariffs; 6. Obtaining the unanimous agreement of various governments to ensure the organization of production and the mutual exchange of various important products.

Judging from the past facts of currency chaos, it is very clear that the first point is the theme of the above six points. We have already said that the stability of currency prices, although not the only condition for restoring the mutual circulation of capital and commodities of various countries, is a necessary condition. However, if the gold standard is not restored, then the abolition of means of managing exchange rates, the elimination of special commercial obstacles, and the stability of tariff policies are all nonsense.

The agenda of the London Conference seems to be very in line with the needs of the times. But we must pay attention to the fact that this is not the achievement of the London Conference. A year ago, when the preparatory work for the London Conference had just begun, many experts had unanimously recognized that this currency issue should be in the most important position, because they believed that currency was the key to all prosperity. They proposed to use a method of reorganizing currency to end the economic panic. Experts have long criticized such one-sided and narrow-minded views as absurd, and there is no need for us to explain them again. A year ago, the currency issue was originally in a secondary position. Unfortunately, since the beginning of 1933, especially since the devaluation of the US dollar, this issue has accidentally aroused special attention from the world and has been regarded as the most important issue. If it is said that the proposals of the London Conference are in line with the needs of the times, this is not based on the farsightedness of the conference's initiators, but rather it can be said that a blind hen sometimes finds a grain of rice!

The experts of the preparatory committee of the London Conference first expressed their attention to the second point on the agenda, namely the issue of preventing the decline in prices. At the same time, some relatively level-headed experts struggled to prevent the conference from aiming solely at raising prices. Because there are some people—this is very painful, but it is an unavoidable fact—who can read and write, can count and calculate, but when it comes to political economy, they are very much like our ancestors, like those ancestors who blindly believed that the sun revolved around the earth, and actually imagined that rising prices could make the world prosperous. I remember Marx saying these words in "The Poverty of Philosophy" (Misère de la philosophie): "When the weather is fine, we can see many people walking in the countryside. Mr. Proudhon wants everyone to go for a walk in order to guarantee that the weather will be fine." Really, that's right, these expert gentlemen, they originally wanted people to go for a walk to restore the fine weather! What could be more foolish than this! We have already anticipated that people who generally advocate using artificial methods to raise prices will definitely do their best at the London Conference, hoping that the conference can decide on this method to restore world prosperity. However, it would not be fair for us to criticize all of these people uniformly, because there are both fetishists and opportunistic people who change their course with the wind. Some of them have a relatively realistic attitude towards the price issue. They believe that even if there is international consensus and a common agreement to devalue all currencies, it may not necessarily be able to revive world prosperity. Let us now study the more realistic new plan of Dauraixi (M. Francis Delaisi).

The proposition of this new plan has long been endorsed by most American economists, and recently, it has been supported by the French economist Dauraixi. He first published his proposal in the journal La République. His concept is different from that of the traveling quacks who generally believe that raising prices can restore prosperity. Based on his article published in La République, we will briefly explain his new plan below:

1. Eliminate various restrictions on currency; 2. Liberate frozen credit; 3. Unify the conversion of foreign debt conditions, using a weaker currency for payment; 4. Eliminate the policy of exchange rate dumping; 5. Abolish commodity quotas, even if they cannot be abolished altogether, at least they must be partially abolished, because such quotas often hinder the outflow of currency; if they are abolished, the factors that hinder currency balance can be reduced; 6. Promote the mutual circulation of capital between countries and make it possible to borrow and invest in foreign countries.

Mr. Dauraixi declared that the new plan he proposed, although it cannot ensure the solution of all the problems of the economic panic, in order to pave the way, it is necessary to first restore the free circulation of capital. Then, we can talk about reducing tariffs and eliminating obstacles to commodity circulation. Mr. Dauraixi has explained his plan in detail as follows:

"There is currently a very difficult reason to solve. Generally, creditors of industrial and commercial enterprises and national creditors all demand more than they have lent. They always believe that they have this sacred right to demand that debtors fulfill the obligations of the total amount of debt on the bill, but estimating the price of these amounts in terms of purchasing power is far greater than the price of the amount borrowed. This entanglement between creditors and debtors originated after the decline in prices in 1929; because since 1929, the global wholesale price index has decreased by an average of about 36%. This means that the purchasing power of money has increased by an average of about 55%. Reducing the price of money has no other meaning than to restore the purchasing power of money to that of 1929, only to enable the numbers in the hands of creditors who receive debts to only obtain the same purchasing power as the amount they lent out. If a miner in California could buy four kilos and eighty-four of goods with one ounce of gold in 1929, today he can buy seven kilos and fifty-seven of goods with the same amount of gold! Therefore, the so-called 'expansion of the purchasing power of gold' has been discovered in the world! The price of gold is much higher than it was four years ago. It is this unreasonable 'expansion' that we are trying to remedy! What should we do? The London Conference should make the governments of all countries decide to simultaneously reduce the amount of gold contained in the currency by 36%. What results can such a unified action achieve? We can say that the gold reserves of all central banks can immediately increase to 55% of the current real price; therefore, the following results can be obtained: (A) Many central banks, whose reserves are only 20% to 25% today, can immediately exceed the legal limits and increase to 30% to 40%, and can further increase the possibility of redeeming their issued banknotes. (B) Banks that are relatively short of gold can also bring them closer to these legal limits, and based on the increase in the amount of currency, they can gradually recover their business. (C) Wealthy banks can lend their surplus gold to the state as a 'public fund' to restore the free circulation of capital and ensure the mutual free action between gold standard countries."

The above words are the content and reasons of Dauraixi's new plan. He seems very cautious and careful, and does not aim at exaggeration. The goals he hopes to achieve are also very limited. This is certainly better than the general quack-style economists who specialize in exaggerating their own glory. However, we must also point out Mr. Dauraixi's mistakes for everyone's research.

Gold is too expensive today, which is the starting point of Dauraixi's theory. Today, to buy the same amount of goods as four years ago, you don't need as much gold as you did four years ago. Dauraixi's argument is indeed an undeniable fact. But unfortunately, it is a huge question whether the devaluation of all currencies (i.e., reducing the gold content in the currency) can remedy this price drop panic.

What is the meaning of currency devaluation and reducing the gold content in the currency? Suppose one ounce of gold (about thirty grams) is minted into two coins: each coin contains fifteen grams of gold. According to Dauraixi's proposal, if we reduce the price of the currency by 36% (approximately one-third of the original price), we must cut one-third of the weight of the original currency. After that, the one ounce of gold used to mint two coins can be minted into three coins: each coin will replace the weight of fifteen grams with a weight of ten grams. Although the currency changes its price in this way, the gold mine owner in California can still continue to buy seven kilos and fifty-seven of goods with one ounce of gold. There is absolutely no change in this matter. Gold is still as expensive as before! However, this one ounce of gold has changed from two fifteen-gram coins to three ten-gram coins. If this lightweight currency and the previous weight currency use the same name, for example, the British gold is still called the pound, and the French currency is still called the franc, then this currency conversion movement will only increase the nominal price by 50%. For example, to buy the same amount of goods, you used to need two coins, but after the currency is devalued by one-third, you need three coins; three coins replace two coins, six coins replace four coins, nine coins replace six coins, and so on. The nominal price has indeed increased by 50%; but after that, the amount of gold contained in three coins is exactly the same as that of the current two coins, so what change has occurred in the relationship between gold and commodities! Originally, there was no change at all! The gold mine owner in California, of course, buys four kilos and eighty-four of goods with two coins in 1933 as he did in 1929, but since his one ounce of gold is worth three coins, the third coin can still buy the remaining amount, and the result is that his one ounce of gold can still buy seven kilos and fifty-seven of goods!

Assuming that Dauraixi's plan can be implemented, can it really achieve the results he hopes for? Can the central banks of various countries really increase the currency price by 55% as a result? Of course, each coin has been cut off one-third of its gold, and the reserves of various central banks can certainly allow the minting of 55% more currency, or the issuance of 55% more supplementary banknotes. If the central banks do not issue supplementary banknotes, then the ratio of their reserves to the banknotes they issue is certainly better than before. But can they check the issuance of banknotes? If it is said that to buy the same amount of goods as before, it is necessary to increase from two coins to three coins, then in order to ensure the circulation of goods, it is necessary to issue more banknotes. Because to make the nominal price fit the amount of the new currency unit after weight reduction after the high rise, the circulating banknotes must also increase by 55%, and the reserves of each bank are still absolutely as insufficient as before. Based on this argument, we can say that points ABC in Dauraixi's conclusion cannot be established.

But the starting point of Dauraixi's theory also has its foothold within a considerable range. After the creditors receive the devalued currency, they can only buy two-thirds of the current goods, just like the same amount in 1929. The debts of industry and commerce can be reduced from this, and the capital of industry and commerce can also be relatively active from this. However, things are not as simple as this: on the one hand, such a reduction in burden may not necessarily increase production, and on the other hand, although the wage laborers who are weakening day by day due to unemployment panic have increased a little nominal wages, they lose more than they gain due to the high prices, and their pain is even worse than in the past; the purchasing power of wage laborers has not only not increased, but even decreased, and it is still a question whether the free circulation of goods and the suitability of production and consumption can be realized.

Currency devaluation is of no benefit to the majority of wage laborers. They have already suffered enough in the fierce waves of the economic panic. Dauraixi's currency devaluation plan does nominally raise prices, but the purchasing power of the majority of people still cannot increase. What remedial effect does this have on the panic of production stagnation and commodity accumulation! The only meaning of his plan is to reduce a little of the gold burden on debtors, especially to reduce the burden on European debtor countries for the United States.

We want to try to come up with a proposal to increase purchasing power at the London Conference, but the result is zero. We believe that the only way to remedy this panic of overproduction and insufficient consumption is to enable the working people to consume the goods they produce. This is the most reasonable remedy. But capital has its own logic, and its logic is based on profit. The main purpose of capitalists in producing various commodities is not to manufacture gifts for wage laborers, but to reap the highest profits! To increase the purchasing power of the masses, it is necessary to increase the wages of wage laborers, and if the wages of wage laborers are increased, it will inevitably lead to a decline in profits. This is ultimately unacceptable to the general capitalists. Therefore, the London Conference, this drama of imperialist infighting, this competition of financial capitalists, will never pay attention to the point of increasing the purchasing power of the masses—currency devaluation and rising prices, although they can superficially beautify and prosper for a while, are ultimately fleeting flowers and are not a fundamental solution to the world economic panic.

Securities

The Bond Market Lacked the Possibility of Progress Last Week 227

Encountered Many Obstacles in the Forward Process ▲

Last week, from August 7th to 12th, the Chinese Securities Exchange, according to the support of the people and the excellence of the environment, and after many days of depression in the previous week, had the possibility of progress. Because it had fallen for many consecutive days, it had been depressed for a long time, and the rebound caused by the reaction, so it was not difficult to break through the highest record of July 19th in a few days. However, because No. 46 in the financial sector continued to sell, it greatly suppressed the prosperous atmosphere of the bond market. Although it struggled, it finally could not rise due to excessive oppression. From this speculation, there should be a violent reaction soon, venting its depressed and rising spirit. Now, the past week will be described in its cliffs and sketches, for reference. On Monday, I observed Feng's telegram, obeying the government's conditions. The inspection suddenly turned downwards, and there was no problem. The recovery of the lost land in North China was also quite smooth. It happened that after many days of falling, and because only two sessions were done in the morning every day, the people unanimously looked high. In the first session, the various gangs entered the stomach extremely eagerly, and the North Gang also rose up to hedge. In one session, it suddenly rose by one or two yuan. The one-eight customs and the majority of September all found new high prices. The various prices in August were almost the same as the highest record on July 19th. Unexpectedly, from the closing of the market, No. 46 immediately sold at a high price, but although it slightly turned small, it still rose by several jiao to one yuan and seventy-eight jiao in one day. The popularity was still strong. On Tuesday, there was no change in the environment, and No. 46 sold even more fiercely. The North Gang saw the opportunity, and the shorts also temporarily waited and stopped hedging. The market price fell continuously for two sessions under high pressure. Financial short-term sales were even more, and the fall was the most severe. It actually fell by several jiao to one yuan and sixty-seven jiao in one day. After this blow, the popularity had dissipated. From Wednesday to Saturday, although the daily results still rose slightly by several jiao, its trend had become a weak and powerless image that would definitely return every time it rose. Because No. 46 still had a small number of sales every day, although the number of jiao on Saturday was extremely clear, it seemed to have nothing to do with the overall rise and fall. Looking at the overall trend of the week, although the rising wind was strong, the oppression was too heavy, so it could not develop. Therefore, the result was only better than the previous week by several jiao to one yuan and sixty-seven jiao. The total number of transactions was calculated to be 61.9693 million yuan, of which the spot was 19,300 yuan. Discussions

On the Future of Female Intellectuals 231

— Bin Fu

A few days ago, this publication carried two articles about the future of intellectuals. In these two articles, the complaints of intellectuals were fully revealed. After reading them, one could not help but sigh deeply. Yes, in such a dark year, the so-called future of intellectuals is out of the question. The dead end of intellectuals is indeed a true and undeniable fact.

However, it suddenly occurred to me that the so-called "intellectuals" here should only refer to men, because I feel that at present, the future of female intellectuals is developing, and the future of female intellectuals is much brighter, at least more so than for "ill-fated" men. Just taking a general observation of the "Self-Employment Introduction" in this publication, women get more "responses" than men, while more men than women submit articles. From this intuitive observation, we can see that in real society, women have a better "fate" than men, or at least it can be said that it is easier for women to find a way out than for men. Therefore, the current "female intellectuals" do not have to "be nannies" as Bai Bijun said. And in fact, this is true: there are college graduates working as waiters; it seems that there are quite a few pulling rickshaws! But I have never heard of a "female intellectual" being a nanny.

Therefore, modern parents, even if they have several seven-foot "men of great talent," may only be able to watch them eat at home in dismay. On the contrary, if they have a beautiful daughter, the parents' "glory and wealth" is "guaranteed." From the results shown in today's society, the idea of "valuing daughters over sons" has undoubtedly become active in the minds of parents.

So someone will ask, what superior conditions do daughters have that make it so easy to find a "way out"? I can answer this directly: "The reason why women can easily find a job (a way out) is simply because they are women." This second "woman" is very difficult to understand. I cannot explain it in detail here. Readers can refer to the "vase" theory published in various newspapers one after another to understand. (The statements about "vases" published in newspapers can probably be compiled into a book.)

"Woman" can become a prerequisite for finding a way out, half due to "talent," and half due to her "intelligence." For example, if "talent" has a defect, she will "intelligently" climb into the rouge jar and somersault to make up for it. (Conversely, if "talent" has special advantages, she will naturally use various methods more cleverly to set it off.) This somersault can naturally open up a "way out"!

Although that's how it is, I can't help but worry about the "female intellectuals" somersaulting in the rouge jar, because if the "rouge-eating" guys disappear from society, even if you somersault a hundred times in the rouge jar, you won't find a "way out."

So, in the final analysis, the future of female intellectuals is really unreliable.

The fact that women seem to have a "way out" now is just a distorted manifestation of the deformed development of a capitalist society.

Male and female intellectuals, you have all reached a dead end. If you want to open up a bright future, use your "intelligence," no! Use your "rouge," no! Only use your "knowledge,"

Use your sweat and strength!

The Way Out for University Graduates 232

— Jie Bai

Five university graduates sat in a narrow and unclean pavilion room discussing the problem of finding a way out that generally plagues modern youth. After talking back and forth, everyone deeply felt that there was no way out for them anywhere in the current society!

Mr. A, who had deeper knowledge and richer abilities, said angrily: The stuff I bought—knowledge—is not bad, but useless, just because the consumer base in today's society is too narrow, which puts us in a dead end.

Mr. B, who had richer social experience, said solemnly: However, the reason why the social consumption base is becoming increasingly narrow is not only due to the oversupply of university graduates, but also the inevitable result of everything in the current society being controlled by those who have no knowledge, academic scoundrels... If you don't believe what I say, then you only need to pay a little attention to the administrative personnel of the Nanjing government and other places. How many of them are university graduates? This can prove that what we say is reality.

Mr. C, who had been subjected to many social stimuli, said very negatively: In short, the characteristic of today's society is that there is no way forward and no way back. In my opinion, we should become monks! Because becoming a monk can not only avoid all the disturbances in the current society, but also live a leisurely and happy life!

Mr. D, who was not very talkative, stood up excitedly and said: I very much agree with Mr. C's opinion of becoming a monk, but I have a statement. If we become monks, we must have the spirit of Christians, that is, we should reform the characteristics of Chinese monks in the past who were scattered and disorganized, and make them organized. In the future, once we have an opportunity, we can lead them to reform Chinese society.

Mr. E, who had a better social science background, seemed to oppose but not oppose, and said with a happy face: I agree with Mr. D's spirit, but I do not agree with the object that Mr. D said—only going to the monk group to organize monks, that is to say, we should expand the spirit of transformation and construction a little, and anyone can be our target, as long as they have the same fate and consciousness as us. Everyone felt that Mr. E's opinion was more appropriate and meaningful, and they all agreed that what he said was the conclusion. At the same time, they also jointly said that they would continue to explore the "bright path" based on Mr. E's conclusion!

Should Live in Widowhood 233

— Jie Xin

"God! Why are you so cruel! You took away my two children! My darling, my child, your mother is calling you so loudly, but you don't answer your mother? My darling, my..."

It was already midnight. A burst of wailing from the kitchen next door woke me up from my dream: followed by this set of painful and sad cries—it was a woman's voice.

That woman, as long as I am aware of her, a shadow of a middle-aged woman with a sharp face, thick lips, bare feet and slippers, long hair, and a button on her chest that is never fastened, who always laughs with a nasal voice when she speaks, will naturally and clearly emerge in my mind. In addition to a husband who spends all day hiding at home "lying on the opium bed" or "cleaning the opium pipe," taking "smoking opium" as a profession, there are also two children living with her—the older one died of dysentery not long ago; the younger one, probably also died in her crying.

The noise last night prevented me from falling asleep in the middle of the night; when dawn was approaching, I got a moment of peace and slept for a while. Probably around ten o'clock, I was still in a hazy and fluttering feeling when suddenly there was a deafening sound of firecrackers outside, which woke me up again. I thought, I don’t know where this dead child has been sent to. As a result, there were many people in the alley discussing it:

"This child was destined to die; how can poor people afford to raise children? Instead of letting the child live in misery, it's better to let this little life be destroyed!"

Another kind of echoing voice is like this: "Originally, this woman was too restless. It was her own fault! After her husband died, she should have taken her two children and lived a good life in widowhood. If she endured some hardship in the present, there would be a glimmer of hope that the children would grow up in the future, but she was unwilling to settle down and insisted on marrying someone else, and she happened to marry such a living treasure. Isn't this her own fault?!"

"..."

"..." They continued to express their opinions on "social customs" and "human hearts" with great enthusiasm, and the tone was extremely indignant and sighing. "Poor people should not have children," what a clever, simple and wonderful conclusion! "Settling down to widowhood" is such a beautiful and humorous deduction! But I didn't understand any of this. What existed in my mind was that humans and all other animals have the same life. They have to eat when they are hungry! Who said that one life has the right to exist and the other life should be destroyed?!...

The Future of the Countryside 234

— Tu Ma

Many people, like the man of Qi worrying about the sky, are making a fuss about "the collapse of the countryside" and "the bankruptcy of the rural economy," but this is actually superficial talk. Some people with "profound knowledge" who understand the situation of the peasants even feel that the extravagant habits of the peasants need to be corrected. Moreover, as long as the rural areas of each province have a large sum of money for reform and revitalization, then in the near future, there is hope for the urbanization of the countryside. With beautiful flowers and brocades, and bright radiance, with great plans, there is no fear of not achieving great things. It all depends on human effort. Now, let's write down the methods to revive the countryside.

(1) Widen the field banks and pave asphalt roads to facilitate the driving of cars.

(2) Fill the river courses and install tap water to save the peasants the trouble of drawing water. And clean drinking water is beneficial to hygiene.

(3) Peasants should abandon the dim oil lamps and kerosene lamps and use electric lights in every household. (4) Build tall western-style houses and dance halls so that peasants can get proper entertainment.

(5) Establish hospitals to protect the lives of peasants and maintain the health of peasants.

(6) Open banks to facilitate peasant savings. (7) Improve the habit of thrift.

(8) Set up detectives to protect the countryside.

(9) Peasants should abandon carrying poles and avoid using sticks, and instead use new-style cargo trucks.

(10) Peasants should not be bareheaded and barefoot, but should dress neatly to enhance their appearance.

Clerk Communication

Each Gets What They Want 235

The Editor:

Every time I read the clerk communication, I see that the answered matters are all detailed and clear, the guidance is well-directed, and the correction is reasonable; from this, it can be known that the editor is not afraid of trouble and has the intention of teaching people tirelessly. Now, I have a trivial matter, please ask you, I hope you will not refuse it.

My father had four brothers. When they separated, the second uncle moved out of the ancestral house, and the eldest and youngest shared an ancestral house. The eldest occupied the east side, and the youngest occupied the west side. The eldest had two sons, and the rooms on the east side were naturally divided between the eldest's two sons; but the eldest's second son had already sold all the rooms he had divided to the youngest. Now, the rooms that the eldest son has divided also want to be sold to the youngest. However, the youngest is short of cash and has no ability to buy them. The eldest and youngest are close relatives, so they proposed that the youngest exchange some good fields for the rooms of the eldest son, which is called exchanging property for property, and signing a mutual exchange contract. I don't know if this method is feasible in terms of legal custom. Please clarify and teach, I am very grateful. Zhao Xueyan bowed respectfully.

Editor's note: The law stipulates that a person has the right to freely dispose of his real estate. The so-called disposal includes use, lease, mortgage, gift, transfer, and sale. Therefore, the youngest exchanging some good fields for the eldest son's real estate is of course a legal act. However, when signing the contract, it is also necessary to ask a witness to be present; afterwards, it is also necessary to assess the price, pay the deed tax, and transfer the household and grain. The closer the relatives, the more proper the procedures must be, so as to avoid disputes caused by doubts from future generations.

This matter is beneficial to both the eldest and youngest. The youngest has three-quarters of the entire house, so he must obtain this one-quarter; since the eldest needs money, a whole pond of good fields is of course easier to exchange than a tangled house; each gets what they want, which is a great suggestion.

Novel

Under the Red and Green Lights (52) 238

— Xi Lin

(28) Third Concubine's Greed: Staring intensely at his retreating figure

After glaring at each other again, Meizi smiled, but Shi Qiao switched to a solemn, serious expression, clearly having made another decision in his heart. He said slowly:

"My dear Meizi, thank you for your encouragement!"

Meizi's face immediately fell, worried that something might have happened.

"Likhanov is waiting for you, go to sleep early." Shi Qiao said these words, clearly restraining his passionate emotions. But immediately, he hugged Meizi tightly, gave her a flurry of passionate kisses, and then pushed her away, asking her to go to sleep. Meizi stood reluctantly at the threshold for a long time, her expression carrying a kind of pious prayer.

After Meizi left, Shi Qiao closed the door and cleaned up his books and letters alone, deciding to leave here and start building a new environment, a new life. In the moment he was cleaning up his things, it was as if he was clearing up his entire life's muddled accounts. All past experiences, thoughts, and feelings came to his mind one by one, and then ended one by one. Then, a kind of childhood joy and youthful aspiration put a smile on his face, and in the smile appeared the heroic countenance of Zhou Shaoping, and that impassioned letter—yes, his words were absolutely right. Good, let all the past die. And look at tonight, the enthusiastic state of the masses, isn't it obvious that the spirit of the old nation is awakening from its yawn, no, waking up with a shout. Regardless of whether the news of Ishikawa's death is true or not, in any case, this enthusiastic situation has given everyone a firm belief in national revival.

As long as the people's hearts have not died completely, as long as history has not been completely corroded, it all depends on us burying our heads and working hard. Really, "Hook Nose" also believes this, "Japan is definitely not our enemy!" He thought, and the things were almost packed. The east was gradually showing a fish-belly color, and the window glass was reflecting a milky white. So he gently carried a few pieces of luggage downstairs to the courtyard steps, because he was afraid of waking Meizi, he wrote a short letter and sealed a month's rent inside, leaving it in the room. Goodbye, my dear Miss Meizi! he shouted in his heart, waving a flying kiss—ah, may my Meizi be happy, and one day gloriously return to her homeland, and that homeland is no longer a den of wolves! Goodbye, dear Meizi, sleep well, he went to the street corner to call for a rickshaw. The street trees on both sides gradually shone with verdant green in the dawn. Suddenly, a car came from the silent distance and stopped unexpectedly in front of him. A woman in bright clothes walked out of the car. This woman was the third concubine. She had the car stop because she saw Li Shi Qiao. Her expression was unusually hurried, but she forced a smile, and even from her slight frown, one could still see the cherry red on her lips. But this only disgusted Li Shi Qiao, and he stood far away without moving. The third concubine walked closer and said:

"Shi Qiao, where are you going so early!"
