Movie Special

The Shadows of Stars (Part 2) 239

— Su Xin

Their understudies are their formidable rivals

The company's tools for controlling stars

One day, a manager at MGM met a young man. Because he looked very much like Gary Cooper, he recruited him and signed a contract with him. He also changed his name for him. He was originally called Archie Leach, and his new name was Cary Grant, which was almost the same as Gary Cooper. The company often gave Cary Grant roles that were similar to Gary Cooper's. However, Gary Cooper was even more mischievous than the managers at the company. He also acted very carefully and cautiously. Whatever they told him to do, he did. This way, Cary Grant had no chance to steal his position.

Because using these "shadows" was a good way for companies to control their stars, not only Paramount or MGM used this method, but other film companies also followed suit. Warner Brothers also had two actors with similar names, faces, and personalities. One was Warner's star, William Powell; the other was Warren William. Once, Powell didn't like the script for "The Mouthpiece", so the company gave the role to William. Later, there was another script for "The Dark Horse" that Powell didn't want to do, so the company gave it to William again. Powell thought both of these plays were absolutely impossible to do well, but William did them just right, turning ordinary stories into brilliant films; his name became famous as a result. Powell had always been very self-important, but now, threatened by this "shadow," he didn't dare to be too reckless.

For the past few years, Paul Muni at Universal Studios has always been dissatisfied with the roles the company has given him. The company felt that he was becoming more and more difficult to control, so they found Kent Douglass, and signed a long-term contract with him. Kent has already proven his acting talent in "Waterloo Bridge" and "A House Divided", and is no less talented than Paul Muni. However, Kent is a stage actor, and he doesn't like making movies, so he left the film industry after his contract expired. But Paul Muni learned his lesson.

Robert Montgomery also has an understudy named Robert Young. He has also proven in films such as "The Merry Widow" that he is not only as elegant as Montgomery, but also natural in his attitude and skilled in his performance, and can completely replace Montgomery. At Metro-Goldwyn-Mayer, there is a Franchot Tone who can also completely replace Clark Gable, who is considered the epitome of masculinity. Clark Gable has been very temperamental lately, and the company feels that he is very difficult to control, but they feel more secure knowing that they have Franchot Tone as his understudy.

Fox is a bit behind in this regard. Charles Farrell left, and they still haven't found someone to replace him. Charles Morton originally had a lot of promise, but his performance was far from satisfactory. They found a Russell Gleason, wanting to use him as a shadow of James Dunn, but the experiment failed.

Ann Harding at RKO is also threatened by this shadow. This shadow is Julie Haydon, whose appearance is very similar to Ann Harding's. In "The Conquerors", Julie played Ann Harding's daughter, and the two were indistinguishable from each other. As for Greta Garbo, there are many good shadows, so there are many American Garbos and German Garbos. But until now, they have not been able to completely defeat this Swedish star. (The End)

Film Review

Review of "Yes, Mr. Brown" 240

— Ling He

Novel subject matter, gorgeous performances,

A top-notch work in opera. - Nanjing Screening

First of all, we are pleased that this opera's subject matter is novel. It uses the theme of satirizing merchants who curry favor with authority. Although performed in the form of a comedy, the kind of situation that makes people laugh and cry is indeed something that makes us have to admire the author's success.

The branch manager, in order to win the favor of the head office's boss, in addition to instructing the store clerks to do their best to please him, also had his wife dress up and accompany him, and host a banquet. But the wife wanted to have her beloved dog accompany her, which was of course inappropriate, so she argued with her husband and angrily took her dog out. The boss suddenly arrived, and the manager had no choice but to temporarily replace his wife with a female secretary. So, although the boss loved the secretary's beauty, he could only leave lightly because she was an employee's wife. Unexpectedly, the wife suddenly returned home because all the theaters had refused to allow her to bring her dog inside. When she learned of this situation, she was very angry, and after her husband explained, she pretended to be the female secretary and appeared before the guest. The general manager then tried to please this fake secretary, and the wife deliberately acted coquettishly to retaliate against her husband. So the husband forced a smile, and it was neither laughing nor crying. Later, in dance halls and nightclubs, he came home drunk, and all the details were completely revealed. So the general manager left with his female secretary, completing the change of scene in the comedy.

As mentioned above, we believe that the success of this opera is definitely not just the gorgeous and perfect performance form, but the profound content of the play. When we read Chekhov's novels, we always feel a spicy bitterness revealed between the lines. Bernard Shaw's works, (Correction: Yesterday's review of "A Flower" in this publication had some errors due to the reporter not having a reference book at the time. The author, Ingland, is a famous director, and this film is his recent work, not his first time directing. We hereby make a correction.) also have the same style, even more sincere and delightful than the former. The so-called irony in laughter and scolding, this kind of laughing sorrow, is precisely where the greatness of the above-mentioned writers lies. Needless to say, literature occupies a major part in film art, so many comedies do not fail entirely because of the chaotic performance, but because the content is too empty, like wearing gorgeous clothes on a paper doll, and there is no guarantee of success. Therefore, the success of this film is determined by the fact that it has quite substantial content, making the play have the possibility of success. We see that although what is written here are some small family matters, the author's depth lies in being able to tightly grasp and fully develop these quite realistic small matters. It can be said that the ugliness of merchants in modern society is very realistically exposed.

The performance is also very consistent with the content. In particular, the form of comedy, and the fact that it is not exaggerated, is even more commendable. Some may say that the branch manager and the female secretary's stumbling steps on the stairs when they return drunk are too restricted by the rhythm of the music. However, this is a prejudice of those who are not accustomed to watching opera. On the contrary, this is precisely a successful scene in this opera. In "Millionaires," we see the same method being used, but because "Millionaires" does not have the unified and lively mood of this film, it is ignored. As for the entire performance, we not only acknowledge that the director has novel methods, but the most important thing is that the mood is not dull or loose. From beginning to end, people feel the sadness of life in loud laughter. In particular, the husband's attitude of watching his wife's intimate behavior in the arms of others, lowering his voice to comfort his wife for a dog but eventually breaking up, falling again and again while dancing in order to please the boss, and finally failing to gain the boss's favor—these, these, the main character Jacob Gannam is truly depicted with depth and detail. The other three supporting actors are also very appropriate.

In this film, we certainly cannot see the slightest bit of positivity, but the small citizen's deep resentment can always win our sympathy. Thus, we must admit that this is a fitting work by a progressive small-citizen artist.

Two Anecdotes by Tian Yi

Making Everyone Poor 241

Tian Yi's previous films mostly had magnificent sets and costumes. Recently, because the subject matter of the scripts has been leaning towards rural areas, the sets and costumes in the films have also greatly changed. The most ridiculous thing is that several actresses, who are usually accustomed to wearing gorgeous clothes, once they change into the attire of rural women, look very peculiar. Like Chen Yumei in "Struggle" and "Auspicious Land," Yuan Meiyun and Wang Huijuan in "Catkins," and Hu Shan and Lu Lixia in "Drifting," and Shao Suxia and Lu Jianfen in "The Adventures of the Little Vagrant," the clothes they wear are, at best, a style of cloth clothing that is out of date. Some are even full of holes, tattered and unbearable. If they weren't filming, they would never put on such ragged clothes again. Hu Shan often said with a laugh, "Boss Shao's calculation is really clever. He thought of this kind of rural play because the cost of adding costumes was too high. Just a few old cloth clothes can save a costume fee, but it makes us all poor."

She's Feeding the Chickens Right Now 242

Since Chen Yumei finished filming "Vitality" and "Struggle," she has been continuously starring in "Auspicious Land." Originally, filming in hot weather is the most distressing thing, but "Auspicious Land" has a lot of outdoor scenes, sometimes in Jiangwan, sometimes in the Lin Family Garden, sometimes in Sanlin Tang, rushing to and fro to film under the scorching sun, which is really a bit unbearable. Now that the outdoor scenes have been filmed, she can take a break, but since she is against dancing and doesn't like swimming, and it's too hot to play basketball or football, she has no way to pass the time, so she can only read novels or play chess with Shao Zuiweng's children. Yesterday, three female students went to visit Chen Yumei. She was wearing a set of black silk shirts and pants, with two short braids behind her head, feeding the little foreign chickens. Although these female students had seen Chen Yumei on the screen, they never expected her to be dressed like this, and thought she was a nanny from the Chen family. So they asked, "Is Miss Chen Yumei at home?" Chen Yumei smiled and said, "She is feeding the chickens right now. May I ask what you ladies need?" The female students felt that this was very humorous, and knowing that this person was Chen Yumei, they became embarrassed and quickly apologized, blaming themselves for not recognizing Mount Tai.

Audience Opinions

My Thoughts on "The Light of Motherhood" 243

— Jie Yu

Yes, domestic films are currently in their nascent stage and need our advocacy and support. However, merely empty praise and irrational adulation will only lead domestic films down the path of gradual degradation and decline.

Like the recent premiere of Lianhua's new film "The Light of Motherhood," many film critics have unanimously praised it as "great," "perfect," "ideologically sound," and "realistic." But where exactly is it great? Where is it sound? Not a single piece of clear evidence can be found in the film reviews, and not the slightest hint of it has been revealed in the film. The company's advertisements proclaim: (1) a deep and penetrating depiction of the greatness of motherhood; (2) a correct awareness of the vanity of women; (3) a severe rebuke to those who worship money; (4) a realistic and detailed exposure of male greed. But these are just claims in the advertisements. These are only very small depictions in the film. Especially the indication of motherhood, committed a serious mistake. Like Huiying is a representative of motherhood, she should show her courage and perseverance in all her expressions, and use an iron will to overcome all difficulties and doubts. Huiying loves her Xiaomei, but why doesn't she have any action to resist Xiaomei's marriage to Huang Shulin; motherly love is only allowing her daughter to develop a habit of vanity. Motherhood in 1933 is probably not so simple.

Secondly, what about Xiaomei's motherhood? Repenting of the past and serving the public. Is doing something in a nursery serving the public? Nurseries are places to take care of children for female workers, but the nursery in "The Light of Motherhood" is like a kindergarten, then Xiaomei, Huiying,... are only working for their own lives, and definitely not serving the public in the nursery. The picture only tells us this.

Thirdly, there are too many coincidences. The chance encounter between Huiying's family and Hu at the concert, the chance that Xiaomei becomes a singer, the chance of a concert to raise funds for the nursery, the chance that Xiaomei marries Huang Shulin and has a daughter and leaves her husband, the chance that she is on stage singing and her little daughter dies, it is true that there is no story without coincidences. These places fully show how far-fetched the story is!

Film Novel "Morning Glory" 6 245

— Ma Teng

Seymour was asking, "Is this the lady?" So Hedges introduced them. Hedges told her that he had already spoken to Seymour, and asked him to help her find some work to do. Seymour very politely and in detail asked her about all her previous experiences. She recited her resume again. Finally, Seymour told her that there was nothing for her to do right now. He asked her to leave her address so that he could contact her in the future. But Irene was unwilling to tell people the unappealing place she was currently living, so she only wrote her name, and said that she would be moving in a day or two, and that she could come again herself. So Hedges led her away. She insisted on going inside to say goodbye to Easton. She told Easton that if Rita Vernon's performance was not satisfactory in the future, he could just call her to replace her. These words made Easton, Sheridan, and others look at each other in confusion, not knowing what she meant.

After Irene Laurance left, Sheridan said to Easton, "I think this woman has something in her belly." Easton glanced at Sheridan and said, "She has a lot of nerve in her belly." But Sheridan remembered her criticism of Rita Vernon being unworthy to perform "Golden Branch," and felt infinite sympathy for her in his heart, and admired that her eye was not bad.

In the months that followed, Irene always remembered the scene when she first met Louis Easton. The days were getting harder and harder, but no one could take away the hope that Irene had from this meeting. She secretly dreamed, thinking that one day, this dream would come true, but for now, she tightened her belt, vowing to be at odds with hunger, and went out every day to seek her path to victory. She also missed Sheridan in her heart, because Sheridan had given her some opportunities. It was a small role, and she felt that she had messed it up, so she didn't want to see him anymore. She sometimes trembled at the inevitability of failure, and was driven by hunger, the hunger for life, the hunger for career, especially the hunger for food. So she had no choice but to accept small things. But the smaller the thing, the harder it was to see her strengths. She often asked herself, would she become famous or not, but she had to become famous immediately.

Winter came again, Irene Laurance's second winter in New York. A dreary cold rain was falling. That evening, Irene slipped out of her apartment to find something to eat. Her purse told her she could only afford a cup of coffee. She ordered a cup of coffee in that dilapidated coffee shop. The warmth of the coffee in her stomach made her feel much more comfortable. She had to pretend that this was a coffee after a full meal. Suddenly, a very familiar voice called her. (To be continued)
